&lt;div xmlns=&quot;http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml&quot; id=&quot;emailbody&quot; style=&quot;margin:0 2em;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt; &lt;table style=&quot;border:0;padding:0;margin:0;width:100%&quot;&gt; &lt;tr&gt; &lt;td style=&quot;vertical-align:top&quot; width=&quot;99%&quot;&gt; &lt;h1 style=&quot;margin:0;padding-bottom:6px;&quot;&gt; &lt;a style=&quot;color:#888;font-size:22px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;font-weight:normal;text-decoration:none;&quot; href=&quot;http://pipes.yahoo.com/pipes/pipe.info?_id=GLEvgE153BGfQ1cmEpPZnA&quot; title=&quot;(http://pipes.yahoo.com/pipes/pipe.info?_id=GLEvgE153BGfQ1cmEpPZnA)&quot;&gt;plus 3, Pruett Holds Off Donohue To Score Second Season Victory - The Auto Chanel&lt;/a&gt; &lt;br /&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;http://fusion.google.com/add?source=atgs&amp;amp;feedurl=http://feeds.feedburner.com/yahoo/FHQZ&quot;&gt; &lt;img style=&quot;padding-top:6px&quot; alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://gmodules.com/ig/images/plus_google.gif&quot; /&gt; &lt;/a&gt; &lt;/h1&gt; &lt;/td&gt; &lt;td width=&quot;1%&quot; /&gt; &lt;/tr&gt; &lt;/table&gt; &lt;hr style=&quot;border:1px solid #ccc;padding:0;margin:0&quot; /&gt; &lt;ul style=&quot;clear:both;padding:0 0 0 1.2em;width:100%&quot; id=&quot;summarylist&quot;&gt; &lt;li&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;#1&quot;&gt;Pruett Holds Off Donohue To Score Second Season Victory - The Auto Chanel&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/li&gt; &lt;li&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;#2&quot;&gt;Panasonic AG-HVX-200 P2 Camcorder Review - Digital Journalist&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/li&gt; &lt;li&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;#3&quot;&gt;New cars tempt shoppers at Rochester auto show - Democrat and Chronicle&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/li&gt; &lt;li&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;#4&quot;&gt;Obituary published March 7 - Sun Chronicle&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/li&gt; &lt;/ul&gt; &lt;table id=&quot;itemcontentlist&quot;&gt; &lt;tr xmlns=&quot;&quot;&gt; &lt;td style=&quot;margin-bottom:0;line-height:1.4em;&quot;&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;margin:1em 0 3px 0;&quot;&gt; &lt;a name=&quot;1&quot; style=&quot;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;font-size:18px;&quot; href=&quot;http://www.theautochannel.com/F/news/2010/03/07/468235.html&quot;&gt;Pruett Holds Off Donohue To Score Second Season Victory - The Auto Chanel&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;font-size:13px;color:#555;margin:9px 0 3px 0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;&quot;&gt; &lt;span&gt;Posted:&lt;/span&gt; 07 Mar 2010 08:12 AM PST&lt;/p&gt; &lt;div style=&quot;margin:0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;div id=&quot;article-text&quot;&gt;&lt;br clear=&quot;all&quot;/&gt;&lt;p&gt;HOMESTEAD, March 7, 2010: Scott Pruett held off a late charge by David Donohue to win Saturday&#39;s Grand Prix of Miami, Round 2 of the GRAND-AM Rolex Sports Car Series presented by Crown Royal Cask No. 16.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Pruett and Memo Rojas scored their second victory in three years at Homestead-Miami Speedway in the No. 01 TELMEX Chip Ganassi Racing with Felix Sabates BMW Riley, holding off the No. 59 Brumos Porsche Riley of Donohue and pole winner Darren Law by .255 seconds.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;In GT, Jeff Segal passed SpeedSource teammate Sylvain Tremblay on the race&#39;s lone restart with 13 minutes remaining and went on to win in the No. 69 FXDD Mazda RX-8. It was the third triumph in the last six races for Segal and Emil Assentato.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&quot;I sure didn&#39;t want to see that last caution, but I was happy for the fans,&quot; Pruett said after scoring his 23rd Rolex Series overall victory. &quot;This is tough competition. You never know what&#39;s going to happen until the checkered flag falls. It was pretty exciting in my seat, that&#39;s for sure.&quot;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Donohue was able to pull up to the back of Pruett several times in the closing laps, but was unable to get by. Pruett managed to weave through GT traffic in the infield on the final lap, and maintained the lead through the superspeedway banking.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Alex Gurney finished third in the No. 99 GAINSCO/Bob Stallings Racing Chevrolet Riley started by Jon Fogarty. Burt Frisselle finished fourth in AIM Autosport&#39;s No. 61 Pacific Mobile Ford Riley, followed by Ryan Dalziel in the debut of the No. 8 Starworks BMW Riley started by Mike Forest, the leading Daytona Prototype Pro-Am driver in the event.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;A turning point came on Lap 81 of the two-hour, 45-minute race. The cockpit of the No. 30 Racers Edge Motorsports Mazda RX-8 exploded into flames, and Jordan Taylor came to a stop in the middle of pit road. The blaze was quickly extinguished and the race remained under green, but Taylor&#39;s car was stopped at the center of the pit lane when Law pitted in the race-leading No. 59 Brumos Racing Porsche Riley.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&quot;There was a car on fire, there were people on pit lane, and I almost came to a stop,&quot; Law explained. &quot;I didn&#39;t want to hit anybody. It&#39;s unfortunate, because I lost all of the gap I had gained. Up until then, I was feeling really, really good.&quot;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Taylor was uninjured in the incident, but the Mazda started by Todd Lamb was eliminated after having a strong run.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&quot;It wasn&#39;t as big a fire as it looked,&quot; Taylor said. &quot;It ended up being some of the insulation in the exhaust catching fire.&quot;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Donohue replaced Law on the ensuing pit stop. Pruett took the lead in the exchange and led the rest of the way.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Pruett and Rojas averaged 107.196 mph, completing 129 laps on the 2.3-mile circuit, and took the points lead by six (67-61) over Ryan Dalziel. The race remained caution-free until Lap 115, for debris in Turns 4 and 8. Law led a race-high 71 laps, followed by Pruett with 48. Other race leaders included Fogarty, who led the opening six laps, and Ryan Hunter-Reay, who led two laps in the No. 95 Level 5 Motorsports BMW Riley.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Rolex 24 At Daytona winners Terry Borcheller and Dalziel each led one lap in different cars. Borcheller was running in contention in the Daytona-winning No. 9 Action Express Racing Porsche Riley. Joao Barbosa, the 2009 Homestead winner seeking his third consecutive Rolex Series victory, went behind the wall early in his shift to replace the heat exchanger.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Tremblay and new regular SpeedSource co-driver Jonathan Bomarito led a GT class leading 44 laps in the Rolex 24 winning No. 70 Castrol Syntec Mazda RX-8.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Tremblay, who led 27 laps, fell back to fourth in the closing laps, but he and Bomarito maintained the points lead by three (63-60) over Robin Liddell and Andrew Davis, who finished second in the No. 57 Stevenson Automotive Group/Vin Solutions Camaro. Finishing third were Leh Keen and James Gue in the No. 41 Dempsey Racing Mazda RX-8.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Bill Auberlen and Joey Hand finished a solid fifth in the No. 94 Turner Motorsport BMW M6. The car ran only three laps in practice prior to the race and did not qualify due to problems with the power steering. Team owner Will Turner installed a power steering unit from a Daytona Prototype prior to the race, and Auberlen and Hand ran in contention throughout the event, with Hand leading four laps.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Paul Edwards started from the GT pole in the Banner Racing No. 07 Mobil 1 Corvette and led the opening 31 laps before turning the car over to motorcycle legend Scott Russell. Edwards returned to the car for the closing shift, finishing sixth - one position ahead of Patrick Dempsey and Joe Foster in the No. 40 Dempsey Racing Mazda RX-8.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Ted Ballou and Andy Lally had the highest-finishing Porsche, placing eighth in the No. 66 AXA Porsche GT3.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;The next race for the GRAND-AM Rolex Series will be the April 10 Porsche 250 at Barber Motorsports Park in Birmingham, Ala.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org&quot;&gt;Five Filters&lt;/a&gt; featured article: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://medialens.org/alerts/09/091216_chilcot_inquiry_the.php&quot;&gt;Chilcot Inquiry&lt;/a&gt;. Available tools: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/pdf-newspaper/&quot;&gt;PDF Newspaper&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/&quot;&gt;Full Text RSS&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/term-extraction/&quot;&gt;Term Extraction&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://thm-a01.yimg.com/nimage/3120e498f2154830&quot; alt=&quot;image&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;This posting includes an audio/video/photo media file: &lt;a href=&quot;http://images.payplay.fm/v/i/victoryseason/600/victoryseason.jpg&quot;&gt;Download Now&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;/div&gt; &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt; &lt;tr&gt; &lt;td style=&quot;margin-bottom:0;line-height:1.4em;&quot;&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;margin:1em 0 3px 0;&quot;&gt; &lt;a name=&quot;2&quot; style=&quot;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;font-size:18px;&quot; href=&quot;http://digitaljournalist.org/issue0603/cameracorner.html&quot;&gt;Panasonic AG-HVX-200 P2 Camcorder Review - Digital Journalist&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;font-size:13px;color:#555;margin:9px 0 3px 0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;&quot;&gt; &lt;span&gt;Posted:&lt;/span&gt; 07 Mar 2010 06:03 AM PST&lt;/p&gt; &lt;div style=&quot;margin:0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;div style=&quot;margin-top:20px;&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;colDropCaps&quot;&gt;I&lt;/span&gt; should begin by pointing out that I&#39;m fairly new to video. My idea of a camera has always been a Leica M6 hanging over my shoulder, and extra rolls of film in my pocket. Now, as a burgeoning documentary maker, I find myself loaded down with bags of lighting, tripods, sound equipment, and cameras. For music videos, I frequently have a whole car full of equipment for multi-camera shoots. That said, I come to the task of evaluating the Panasonic HVX-200 with a particular point of view. I like simple, rugged cameras that produce gorgeous pictures. The HVX-200 is in my comfort zone.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;First the ergonomics: The HVX is beefy. It feels bigger than the other cameras I&#39;ve used but also seems much better balanced. It&#39;s got an industrial, almost military feel about it. Before using the HVX, I&#39;d been shooting with a Canon XL-1 and XL-2 so I&#39;ll be comparing a bit with the controls and features of these cameras. Users of Panasonic DVX cameras will be much more at home with the HVX. It looks, feels and operates like a chunky DVX-100. Compared to the Canons, the HVX-200 is more handheld and less shoulder-mount. It also feels more compact, like a cube. There are fewer adornments sticking out. I personally like this a lot. The camera fits in a smaller case than the XL-2 and feels more rugged as I&#39;m carrying it around.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;My shooting style is mostly manual and the HVX makes this very comfortable. The focus ring is smooth: although I&#39;d prefer a physical stop on it. There&#39;s an auto-manual focus button just behind the lens. When set to manual, you can give it a momentary push to zoom-to-infinity. Below this button is a momentary button to force an autofocus. Above the auto-manual switch is a focus-assist button, which opens a zoomed-in window on the viewfinder to obtain a sharper manual focus. I found this effective, although I could focus a bit easier using the EVF rather than the LCD screen.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;The fixed-mount lens itself is a Leica Dicomar 13X with a 35mm equivalent range of 32mm to 422mm. Century Optics is shipping a .6 wide-angle adapter and 1.6 tele-adapter with a full-zoom .75 adapter and fisheye adapter to follow. These would give you an effective 35mm range in your bag of 19mm to 675mm. All in all, the lens quality is excellent and the add-ons sufficiently flexible that I don&#39;t believe I&#39;ll miss having a removable lens. To my eye, the lens shows no objectionable qualities at any aperture. I tried the Century Optics .6 adapter, which snaps on the front of the lens in place of the lens hood, and I found minimal vignetting and an acceptable level of barrel distortion, given the very wide angle of view.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;/&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;The Iris Control (I&#39;ll always think of it as aperture) is a knurled knob on the left side of the camera just behind the lens. It is large enough to be easily accessible. The F-stop is displayed in the viewfinder so you can adjust the iris without ever taking the camera from your eye. This is a consistent characteristic with all controls on this camera. From my still camera use, I have always preferred a camera such as a Leica that has controls that can be differentiated by touch rather than requiring that you actually look at the knobs and buttons. I want to be able to operate the camera manually and make any adjustments quickly and by feel. I find the ergonomics of the HVX-200 very satisfying in this regard. All controls are large, well-placed and well-thought-out. Although this camera has an enormous amount of flexibility in its adjustments, I find that the controls on the outside of the camera are ones that I am always using. There&#39;s nothing superfluous and the controls are clustered by function. For example, right over the Iris knob is the ND switch, and just behind the knob is an auto-manual Iris button. When the aperture is set to auto, you can still adjust it manually with the knob, but when the light changes auto will take over and reset the F-stop.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;The three-position switch for Neutral Density ND 1/64, 1/8 and off corresponding to 7.5, 3 and 0 stops of light reduction. I find that I use this frequently to reduce depth of field. One of the biggest weaknesses of this camera, as with all 1/3&quot; CCD cameras, is that it&#39;s very hard to throw the background out of focus unless you get very far away from your subject. Conversely, 2/3&quot; CCD cameras use longer lenses for an equivalent field of view, and therefore offer more depth of field control. About all you can do with the 1/3&quot; CCD cameras is open the aperture wide, go to a faster shutter or ND, shoot at maximum zoom, and hope for the best.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;The zoom ring is large, and in manual mode, is very smooth. With the XL2 I normally zoomed manually for focusing and used power zoom to get a smooth zoom effect while shooting. This is more problematic with the HVX since you need to disengage the power zoom to easily turn the manual zoom ring. Maybe I&#39;m supposed to do this with the XL2 but I&#39;ve never bothered. Here it&#39;s pretty mandatory since it feels like you are forcing the motor if you don&#39;t disengage. On the other hand, I&#39;ve started using a Manfrotto control for most of my shooting. On sticks, I&#39;m using the 522P camera control, which has three zoom speeds as well as progressive and constant zoom. On my Fig Rig, I&#39;m using the 521P controller. Both offer me enough flexibility that I haven&#39;t been using manual zoom on this camera. Also, the power zoom seems much quieter than other cameras I&#39;ve used. I&#39;ve yet to hear the motor, even in a very quiet scene. The degree of zoom can be displayed in the viewfinder as either Z0-Z99, feet and inches, or meters. I haven&#39;t decided which I prefer yet, but it&#39;s nice to have the flexibility.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;One nice feature of the viewfinder is that the 16x9 image is displayed inside a 4:3 frame. So data like aperture, zoom, shutter speed, etc. is displayed mostly above and below the image. This makes it much easier to leave this data showing and still see enough of your scene to shoot.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;At the bottom of the camera there are three buttons labeled USER1, USER2 and USER3. These can be used as shortcuts for settings, such as fade in and fade out. Frankly, I don&#39;t find these buttons very useful. I would much rather see them be able to do functions like remember a zoom position, or remember a focus setting.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;Behind the flip-out 3.5&quot; viewfinder, there are more controls including shutter speed select, SMPTE color bar generator, Time Code settings, Image Stabilizer on/off, Zebra mode, and audio input selections.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;Once again, these controls can be operated by feel without ever taking the camera away from your eye. The shutter speed is displayed in the viewfinder, along with F-stop and focus distance. The time code can be set to either free run or to advance only while recording. Free run is particularly useful in a two-camera shoot such as a music video, where you zero the TC in both cameras when you start, leave one camera running to record the audio and a full event long shot, and then use the second camera to start/stop on close-ups. The consistent time code between the two cameras will greatly assist in the editing. There is also a provision to synchronize the time code of multiple cameras over the Firewire connection.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;The camera has the familiar image controls found in the current generation of high-end consumer and professional cameras. These include Chroma Level and Phase for subtle color palette adjustment, Detail Level for crisper or softer edges, Detail Coring for noise control, Color Temp for coarse color correction, Master Pedestal for controlling the range of blacks, Gamma for controlling the dynamic range curve, and Matrix for either subtly brightening colors or fine tuning the color curve for fluorescent lights, and Knee to control what happens to blown out whites. There&#39;s also a Skin Detail control, been referred to sometimes as &quot;Barbara Walters Mode,&quot; which is effective at softening skin wrinkles. These settings are associated with one of six named Scene settings. These settings can be saved to an SD card. I&#39;m already building up a little kit of SD cards with settings to match different shooting situations.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;White balancing is a simple one-button push of the AWB button on the front of the camera. Be sure to carry a white card and you&#39;ll get great color. You can also save two white balance settings (A or B). There is also an Auto Tracking White feature to gradually change the white balance to changing conditions. I&#39;m not a big fan of this feature but I can see the value. If you didn&#39;t bring your white card, there are two fixed settings for 3200K halogen light or 5600K outdoor light. Panasonic recommends that you periodically adjust the black balance. You do this while not recording by setting the white balance and then holding the AWB button longer to reset the black balance.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;In addition to the image settings, the Scene settings also include setting the camera to Video Mode or Film Camera mode. When this is set to Film Cam and the Recording Format is set to one of the 720-line progressive settings (720P), then the Frame Rate can be set to a range of 12 through 60. For example, if you are shooting in 720/24p and the Frame Rate is set to 60, it&#39;s called &quot;overcrank&quot; and, when played back, your video is played in slow motion. If set to a low setting, such as 12, you will get an &quot;undercranked&quot; shot which plays back twice as fast as reality.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;This feature is a hoot. Before I used it, I thought of variable frame rate as yet another in-camera gimmick like fades and wipes. However, I&#39;m now a convert. Beyond the obvious super-smooth slow motion action shots, I found that a bit of slo-mo is very useful for getting nice steady handheld scenic shots. And a bit of undercrank makes for very dramatic action shots of, for example, skiers or motorcycle jumps or car chases. I tried some slow motion (overcranked) shots of the surf and snow during a recent blizzard. The interesting thing about these is that you don&#39;t notice during playback that they are not recorded at normal speed. Just seems like the waves are more dramatic and the snowflakes are more visible. I never realized how powerful changing the speed of non-people shots can be when done subtly. The terms, incidentally come from the days of manual film cameras, if you crank the film fast and get more frames per second then you have slow motion when it&#39;s played normally. The opposite happens when you undercrank.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;I expected to have problems with a stroboscopic effect on pans, as I&#39;ve seen when shooting at 24 on the XL2. Either I&#39;ve been lucky so far or the Panasonic is just a lot better at 24 fps but my fast pans with this camera have been very pleasantly smooth.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;Unlike some other HDTV cameras, which are optimized for 1080 interlaced video compressed to HDV recording format, the HVX-200 is optimized for 720-line progressive scan video recorded to DVCPRO HD. A major difference with the HVX-200 is that the output is recorded with far less compression than with the various HDV cameras. The HVX records at 100 mbits/second as opposed to 25 mbits/second for HDV. For a recording with little motion, the two approaches (HDV versus DVCPRO HD) will both give beautiful pictures. The advantage of Panasonic&#39;s approach lies with the ability to capture far more action in the shots. This difference can be graphically illustrated by showing a rapid pan shot with both cameras. Very often with HDV you&#39;ll see some breakup or pixelation in the image while the Panasonic video will be rock solid. This is the &quot;satellite TV&quot; effect, in that it&#39;s much like watching a football game on satellite TV in a snowstorm. Another advantage of the HVX recording method is that it records 4-2-2 color rather than 4-2-0 color sampling as HDV does. The practical result of this is that there is much more color information available for better color correction in post. Yet another advantage of DVCPRO HD is that there is no inter-frame (or temporal) compression. So editing is far less work for your computer. With HDV, your computer has to uncompress each compressed frame sequence in order to regenerate the frames for editing.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;According to Panasonic, the HVX operates natively in 1080p mode, meaning that it is capturing 1080 horizontal lines sequentially (not interlaced). However, it does not record 1080p. The choices of recording formats with this camera are extensive. It supports nine High Definition modes (1080 or 720 lines) and twelve Standard Def modes (480 lines). Recording takes place in DVCPRO HD at 100 mbits/second, DVCPRO 50 (50mbits), DVCPRO 25, and DV. Both 16:9 and 4:3 aspect ratios are supported. I believe that this has more flexibility than any other camcorder regardless of price. I also believe that the horizontal resolution is as good or better than any other 1/3&quot; CCD camcorder and most 2/3&quot; camcorder. The only major limitations of this camcorder versus a $65,000 Varicam appear to be low-light performance, depth-of-field, and ability to change the frame rate while recording.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;The HVX-200 records on P2 memory cards at its maximum resolution, streams over Firewire at 720 lines or below, or records normal miniDV tapes. The P2 cards are PCMCIA form factor cards which can be directly inserted into a laptop for accessing like a hard drive. The cards come in 8GB or 4GB size currently, although a 16GB card is rumored and Panasonic has estimates that 128GB cards will be available within the next couple years. With the 720/24PN setting, an 8GB card will hold 21 minutes of recording. The camera holds two cards and the cards can be hot-swapped without stopping recording. So with enough cards, or with a laptop or Panasonic&#39;s P2 Store, you can record indefinitely.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;/&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;There&#39;s been a lot of discussion about the pros and cons of P2 cards versus tape. At 1080/60i your recording time without swapping cards is short, 16 minutes with two 8GB cards. For event photography this would appear to be a severe limitation. If you must have 1080i and you are doing primarily unattended shooting or don&#39;t want to deal with hot-swapping cards while shooting, then this is probably not the right camera for you. If you find, like me, that 720p looks at least as good as 1080i then don&#39;t worry about the record time. Swapping cards works just fine and you always have the option of direct recording to hard drive via Firewire. If you don&#39;t want to make the investment in at least two or three 8GB P2 cards, then I don&#39;t recommend the camera unless you are planning to record only via Firewire or you are going to use the camera as an SD camera until you can afford the P2 cards.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;Transferring the cards to a G4 Powerbook is a pleasure. From Final Cut Pro you select &quot;Import... Panasonic P2&quot; from the File menu. A window shows you each clip and you can select which ones to import. I&#39;ve found that I can &quot;capture&quot; a couple hours of video in less than a half hour. Surprisingly, the P2 Store appears to be a bit slower copying but still is fast enough to have the card ready for recording by the time you&#39;ll need it.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;My shooting mode with this camera is to stick with 720/24PN recording mode going to the P2 cards. This maximizes my recording time, lets me take advantage of over- and undercrank, lets me stream simultaneously to Firewire, and gives me beautiful softer film-like video. I also shoot with Cine-Like-D Gamma because I prefer an extended dynamic range with a bit softer saturation. You can call it Film Look versus Reality TV, or Erotic versus Graphic depending on your market. Mastering the Scene settings is clearly the longest learning curve with this camera but has a big payoff in achieving the results you want. With your personal Scene kit on SD, you&#39;ll never need another lens filter (except maybe a polarizer).&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;One caution when recording in Cine-Like Gamma: There&#39;s expanded dynamic range but Knee is disabled so there&#39;s nothing to prevent blown-out highlights. Be sure to turn on the Zebra and keep a close watch on the highlights.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;The HVX-200 is capable of recording fantastic audio. While recording onto P2 Cards, the camera always records four channels of 16-bit audio sampled at 48KHz. Two of these are XLR inputs for external mics and two are the onboard mic. Phantom power is available for the XLRs. The A/D conversion and filters are excellent. My only gripe is that you can only set and view the levels on channel 1 and 2. So to get 4 useable channels, you need to set your levels for channel 3 and 4 and then adjust your input levels for 1 and 2 externally if possible. There should at least be some sort of a level balance in the Menu items. &amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;The headphone output can be set to either input or frame-delayed recorded output. You may find the latter annoying, as you&#39;ll hear the output as an echo of reality. I use Bose noise-canceling headphones so I don&#39;t hear anything but what&#39;s going to tape. For playback, the camera speaker is surprisingly loud. At a recent shoot, I reviewed a shot and had the whole room turn to look for the boom box culprit.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;Shooting with this camera is a wonderful experience. It&#39;s a sturdy, well-thought-out machine that lets you quickly adapt to changing situations. For the manual shooter, everything is in the right place, easy to use, and visible in the viewfinder. The pictures you take will be mind-blowing. Which brings up another important consideration of shooting with this camera or with HD in general. This is an unforgiving medium. Focus, motion, color, lighting are all much more critical than with SD broadcast recording. Lighting is especially critical with 1/3&quot; CCD cameras since the light sensitivity is less than with 2/3&quot; cameras or some DV cameras. Bring lights or find light. Your available low light shots may be disappointing. &amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;Focus and camera motion are also more critical. I am not a steady camera handler by nature. I use sticks as much as I can and I use a Fig Rig coupled with an attached monopod for most of my &quot;handheld&quot; shooting. This works for me. Although I find the HVX easier to hold and better balanced than the XL2, the HD output puts a much greater demand on good shooting. This is a hefty camera at almost seven pounds with battery. It supposedly just barely works on a Steadicam Merlin if you paste a couple quarters on the counter balance. I recommend getting a sturdier tripod than you might use with a DVX100 or XL2. I had been using a Libec M20 with my XL2 but for the HVX-200 I&#39;ve acquired a much sturdier Manfrotto 3182, 510 head, and the previously mentioned 522P control arm. One nice feature of this setup is that I have a compatible quick release on the tripod and Fig Rig.&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;/&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;colBody&quot;&gt;The HD Revolution has reached critical mass. The demand for high-definition video is growing dramatically and the ability to provide HD can provide a significant competitive edge to the independent producer. Of the under $10K high-definition cameras that have been introduced, the HVX-200 is in a class by itself. It is better compared to the $65K cameras that are its genetic heritage. After shooting with this camera for a couple weeks, I don&#39;t want to go back. It&#39;s the first video camera that I&#39;ve used that gives me the kind of image quality that I have cherished in film. It&#39;s also the first video camera that I&#39;ve used that gives me the ergonomics, engineering and construction of the very best still cameras.&lt;/p&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org&quot;&gt;Five Filters&lt;/a&gt; featured article: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://medialens.org/alerts/09/091216_chilcot_inquiry_the.php&quot;&gt;Chilcot Inquiry&lt;/a&gt;. Available tools: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/pdf-newspaper/&quot;&gt;PDF Newspaper&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/&quot;&gt;Full Text RSS&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/term-extraction/&quot;&gt;Term Extraction&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;image&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt; &lt;tr&gt; &lt;td style=&quot;margin-bottom:0;line-height:1.4em;&quot;&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;margin:1em 0 3px 0;&quot;&gt; &lt;a name=&quot;3&quot; style=&quot;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;font-size:18px;&quot; href=&quot;http://www.democratandchronicle.com/article/20100307/NEWS01/3070336/1003&quot;&gt;New cars tempt shoppers at Rochester auto show - Democrat and Chronicle&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;font-size:13px;color:#555;margin:9px 0 3px 0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;&quot;&gt; &lt;span&gt;Posted:&lt;/span&gt; 07 Mar 2010 04:59 AM PST&lt;/p&gt; &lt;div style=&quot;margin:0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;div id=&quot;GPage1&quot; class=&quot;gel-pane gpagediv&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;pp&quot;&gt;Rob Rebstein of Brighton was checking out the new cars at the Rochester International Auto Show on Saturday, but he wasn&#39;t planning on buying.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p/&gt;&lt;p&gt;It was the second year that Rebstein, who was with his cousin, Brian Bailey of Fairport, has been at the auto show, which was held at the Riverside Convention Center.&lt;span class=&quot;aa&quot;&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p/&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;pp&quot;&gt;&quot;I&#39;m just getting some ideas,&quot; said Rebstein, 25, who said he prefers American cars, like Ford and Chevrolet. &quot;I like to come here and see the new stuff. But I&#39;m just looking. Most of it is eye candy.&quot;&lt;span class=&quot;aa&quot;&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;pp&quot;&gt;Plenty of customers were whipping out their camera phones and snapping shots of cars like the Chevrolet Corvette ZR1, with a sticker price of $121,980, and the Mercedes S550 sedan, which was going for $94,600. There were also plenty of hybrids and sport-utility vehicles, and more unusual rides such as a handicap-accessible &quot;trike,&quot; which allows wheelchair-bound people to drive a motorcycle.&lt;span class=&quot;aa&quot;&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;pp&quot;&gt;Brad McAreavy, president of the Rochester Auto Dealers Association, said some folks were just looking, but others were shopping.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p/&gt;&lt;p&gt;He said 2009 was the first year in recent memory when new-car sales were topped by &quot;scrappage&quot; vehicles â those that conk out or die â which he said creates a &quot;pent-up demand&quot; for sales.&lt;span class=&quot;aa&quot;&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;pp&quot;&gt;He also said last year&#39;s &quot;Cash for Clunkers&quot; program did not exhaust the market for new-car buyers, but instead got gas guzzlers off the road and kept buyers interested in new cars â and manufacturers producing more fuel-efficient vehicles.&lt;span class=&quot;aa&quot;&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;pp&quot;&gt;One of the potential shoppers was Karess Rowe of Chili, who said she planned to buy within a few months. She had her eye on the Acura TSX, the Hyundai Tucson and the GMC Terrain.&lt;span class=&quot;aa&quot;&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;pp&quot;&gt;&quot;Of course, I&#39;m also looking at the cars that I can&#39;t purchase,&quot; said Rowe, 23, with a smile.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p/&gt;&lt;p&gt;&quot;But it&#39;s nice to dream.&quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p/&gt;&lt;p&gt;Rowe&#39;s mother, Sharon Rowe of Rochester, was checking out some eye candy â a Lincoln MKX, with a sticker price of $40,695.&lt;span class=&quot;aa&quot;&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;pp&quot;&gt;&quot;I&#39;m a little tempted,&quot; she said. &quot;But my car is only a year-and-a-half old.&quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p/&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;mailto:AMORRELL@DemocratandChronicle.com&quot;&gt;AMORRELL@DemocratandChronicle.com&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;aa&quot;&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org&quot;&gt;Five Filters&lt;/a&gt; featured article: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://medialens.org/alerts/09/091216_chilcot_inquiry_the.php&quot;&gt;Chilcot Inquiry&lt;/a&gt;. Available tools: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/pdf-newspaper/&quot;&gt;PDF Newspaper&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/&quot;&gt;Full Text RSS&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/term-extraction/&quot;&gt;Term Extraction&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;image&quot;&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt; &lt;tr&gt; &lt;td style=&quot;margin-bottom:0;line-height:1.4em;&quot;&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;margin:1em 0 3px 0;&quot;&gt; &lt;a name=&quot;4&quot; style=&quot;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;font-size:18px;&quot; href=&quot;http://www.thesunchronicle.com/articles/2010/03/07/obituaries/7062209.txt&quot;&gt;Obituary published March 7 - Sun Chronicle&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;font-size:13px;color:#555;margin:9px 0 3px 0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;&quot;&gt; &lt;span&gt;Posted:&lt;/span&gt; 06 Mar 2010 11:15 PM PST&lt;/p&gt; &lt;div style=&quot;margin:0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;tablecontent&quot;&gt;&lt;div align=&quot;center&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &amp;#13;  &lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; &amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &lt;br /&gt;&amp;#13; &amp;#13; &lt;br /&gt;A local obituary was published Sunday, March 7 for: Robert K. Casavant Sr., 87, of Wrentham.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Robert K. Casavant Sr., 87&lt;b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;WRENTHAM&lt;/b&gt; - Robert K. Casavant Sr., 87, of 119 Thurston St., died peacefully early Saturday morning at the Pond Home in Wrentham. He was the loving and devoted husband of the late Helen (Beaudro) Casavant.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Born in Richford, Vt. on Oct. 30, 1922, he was a son of the late Clarence and Grace (Shattuck) Casavant. Educated in Boston schools, he was a graduate of the Boston Trade School.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A proud veteran, he had served our nation in the United States Army during World War II.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Mr. Casavant was a retired auto mechanic, and had worked for many years maintaining and repairing the fleet of the U.S. Postal Service in Boston.&amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; An avid antique car enthusiast, he loved car shows and was at one time a very active member of the South Shore Antique Auto Club. He and his wife also very much enjoyed motorcycle riding and had traveled throughout the Northeast and Canada.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Formerly of Stoughton and Mission Hill, Bob and Helen had moved their family to Wrentham in 1960.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;He is survived by his loving children: Robert K. Casavant Jr. of Wrentham, and Beth V. Caddell of Bishop, Calif.; a dear sister, Janice O&#39;Neil of Norwood; four devoted grandchildren; and five great-grandchildren.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Relatives and friends are invited to visit with his family at the home of his son Robert Casavant Jr., 40 Ray Road, Wrentham, today, Sunday, March 7 from 1 to 4 p.m.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;No further services are planned at this time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Arrangements are in the care of Richard Ross and the RJ Ross Funeral Home, Wrentham Center, &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://www.rjrossfuneralhomeinc.com&quot;&gt;www.rjrossfuneralhomeinc.com&lt;/a&gt;.&amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Â &lt;/p&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;p&gt;&lt;br class=&quot;clear&quot;/&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org&quot;&gt;Five Filters&lt;/a&gt; featured article: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://medialens.org/alerts/09/091216_chilcot_inquiry_the.php&quot;&gt;Chilcot Inquiry&lt;/a&gt;. &lt;div xmlns=&quot;http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml&quot; id=&quot;emailbody&quot; style=&quot;margin:0 2em;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt; &lt;table style=&quot;border:0;padding:0;margin:0;width:100%&quot;&gt; &lt;tr&gt; &lt;td style=&quot;vertical-align:top&quot; width=&quot;99%&quot;&gt; &lt;h1 style=&quot;margin:0;padding-bottom:6px;&quot;&gt; &lt;a style=&quot;color:#888;font-size:22px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;font-weight:normal;text-decoration:none;&quot; href=&quot;http://pipes.yahoo.com/pipes/pipe.info?_id=GLEvgE153BGfQ1cmEpPZnA&quot; title=&quot;(http://pipes.yahoo.com/pipes/pipe.info?_id=GLEvgE153BGfQ1cmEpPZnA)&quot;&gt;plus 3, Law Wins Pole For Grand Prix Of Miami - The Auto Chanel&lt;/a&gt; &lt;br /&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;http://fusion.google.com/add?source=atgs&amp;amp;feedurl=http://feeds.feedburner.com/yahoo/FHQZ&quot;&gt; &lt;img style=&quot;padding-top:6px&quot; alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://gmodules.com/ig/images/plus_google.gif&quot; /&gt; &lt;/a&gt; &lt;/h1&gt; &lt;/td&gt; &lt;td width=&quot;1%&quot; /&gt; &lt;/tr&gt; &lt;/table&gt; &lt;hr style=&quot;border:1px solid #ccc;padding:0;margin:0&quot; /&gt; &lt;ul style=&quot;clear:both;padding:0 0 0 1.2em;width:100%&quot; id=&quot;summarylist&quot;&gt; &lt;li&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;#1&quot;&gt;Law Wins Pole For Grand Prix Of Miami - The Auto Chanel&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/li&gt; &lt;li&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;#2&quot;&gt;Mercury News interview: Sergio Santos, president of UAW Local 2244 - San Jose Mercury News&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/li&gt; &lt;li&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;#3&quot;&gt;Honda picks Rajasthan over Haryana - Central Chronicle&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/li&gt; &lt;li&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;#4&quot;&gt;MANDARIN COPS: Shoplifter caught after store employee bitten and ... - Florida Times-Union&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/li&gt; &lt;/ul&gt; &lt;table id=&quot;itemcontentlist&quot;&gt; &lt;tr xmlns=&quot;&quot;&gt; &lt;td style=&quot;margin-bottom:0;line-height:1.4em;&quot;&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;margin:1em 0 3px 0;&quot;&gt; &lt;a name=&quot;1&quot; style=&quot;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;font-size:18px;&quot; href=&quot;http://www.theautochannel.com/F/news/2010/03/06/468185.html&quot;&gt;Law Wins Pole For Grand Prix Of Miami - The Auto Chanel&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;font-size:13px;color:#555;margin:9px 0 3px 0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;&quot;&gt; &lt;span&gt;Posted:&lt;/span&gt; 06 Mar 2010 08:35 AM PST&lt;/p&gt; &lt;div style=&quot;margin:0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;div id=&quot;article-text&quot;&gt;&lt;br clear=&quot;all&quot;/&gt;&lt;p&gt;HOMESTEAD, March 6, 2010: Darren Law - with some help from Brumos Racing official Hurley Haywood - ran a lap of 1:11.806 (115.311 mph) to capture the pole for Saturday&#39;s Grand Prix of Miami, Round 2 of the GRAND-AM Rolex Sports Car Series presented by Crown Royal Cask No. 16.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Law led a nine-driver assault on Jon Fogarty&#39;s five-month-old Homestead-Miami Speedway Daytona Prototype track record in preparation for the two-hour, 45-minute race that takes the green flag at 5 p.m. ET Saturday (SPEED, live).&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Paul Edwards won the GT pole in the No. 07 Mobil 1 Corvette with a lap of 1:18.123 (106.322 mph). Eight drivers were under Nick Ham&#39;s 2009 track mark in the 15-minute session.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Fogarty qualified second in the No. 99 GAINSCO/Bob Stallings Racing Chevrolet, 1:11.839 (114.311 mph), followed by Brian Frisselle in the No. 6 The Pit Stop on Norris Lake Ford Riley, 1:12.079 (114.874 mph); Memo Rojas in the No. 01 TELMEX BMW Riley, 1:12.166 (114.735 mph); and Ricky Taylor in the No. 10 SunTrust Ford Dallara, 1:12.282 (114.551 mph).&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Also eclipsing the former track record were Ryan Hunter-Reay in the No. 95 Crown Royal Cask No. 16/US Bank BMW Riley, Mark Wilkins in the No. 61 Pacific Mobile Ford Riley, Buddy Rice in the No. 90 Spirit of Daytona Porsche Coyote, and Rolex 24 At Daytona winner Terry Borcheller in the No. 9 Action Express Racing Porsche Riley.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Haywood won last October&#39;s Grand Prix as a late substitute in the No. 59 Brumos Racing Porsche Riley, co-driving with Joao Barbosa. One of America&#39;s most successful endurance racers, Haywood retired from active competition following the season-opening Rolex 24 At Daytona - a race he won a record five times. He remains active in the sport as an official with Brumos Racing.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&quot;Prior to going out, Hurley told me to get in the car and visualize the track,&quot; said Law, who won his only prior pole position at Homestead-Miami Speedway in 2005. &quot;I kind of blew it off, but I did get in the car early and tried to visualize it. Then we went out and won the pole, and Hurley&#39;s taking all the credit for it.&quot;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Fogarty had a personal streak of winning the pole in his last five qualifying attempts, while he ended 2009 by winning the pole in six of the last seven races, including the finale at Homestead-Miami Speedway.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&quot;We would like to be on the pole, but it&#39;s a good starting position,&quot; said Fogarty, who shared the 2007 and 2009 Daytona Prototype championships with Alex Gurney. &quot;I&#39;m a little disappointed that we didn&#39;t maximize qualifying, but we were also trying to conserve our tires and not put a lot of laps on them. We only ran one quick lap. The Brumos guys are right there and super fast. &quot;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Edwards and Banner Racing won the GT class in three of its last four Homestead races in a Pontiac. Edwards will be joined on Saturday by Scott Russell in the No. 07 Mobil 1 Corvette, with the motorcycle legend missing Friday&#39;s Homestead activities to participate in SPEED&#39;s coverage of the Daytona 200 By Honda - America&#39;s premier motorcycle race. Russell won that event five times.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&quot;We couldn&#39;t do three laps in a row at Daytona without it breaking down,&quot; said Edwards. &quot;Today, we ran all day without a problem. The car&#39;s fast. We&#39;re getting the car very well balanced. The team&#39;s done a remarkable job to get the car where we didn&#39;t have a hiccup in it. That gives me a lot of confidence.&quot;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;SpeedSource claimed the next three positions and Mazda the next four. Jonathan Bomarito made his qualifying debut as regular co-driver in the Rolex 24 class-winning SpeedSource No. 70 Castrol Syntec Mazda RX-8 by winning the outside pole with a lap of 1:18.132 (105.975 mph).&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;John Edwards qualified third in the debut of the SpeedSource No. 68 Nuclear Clean Air Energy Mazda RX-8, 1:18.137 (105.968 mph), followed by Emil Assentato in the SpeedSource No. 69 FXDD Mazda, 1:18.144 (105.958 mph) and Todd Lamb in the No. 30 Racers Edge Motorsports Mazda RX-8, 1:18.219 (105.857 mph).&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Also under Ham&#39;s old track record were Andrew Davis in the No. 57 Stevenson Automotive Group/Vin Solutions Camaro, James Gue in Dempsey Racing&#39;s No. 41 Global Diving Mazda RX-8 and Luke Hines in the No. 48 Miller Barrett Racing Porsche GT3.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org&quot;&gt;Five Filters&lt;/a&gt; featured article: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://medialens.org/alerts/09/091216_chilcot_inquiry_the.php&quot;&gt;Chilcot Inquiry&lt;/a&gt;. Available tools: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/pdf-newspaper/&quot;&gt;PDF Newspaper&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/&quot;&gt;Full Text RSS&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/term-extraction/&quot;&gt;Term Extraction&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;image&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt; &lt;tr&gt; &lt;td style=&quot;margin-bottom:0;line-height:1.4em;&quot;&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;margin:1em 0 3px 0;&quot;&gt; &lt;a name=&quot;2&quot; style=&quot;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;font-size:18px;&quot; href=&quot;http://www.mercurynews.com/business/ci_14520025&quot;&gt;Mercury News interview: Sergio Santos, president of UAW Local 2244 - San Jose Mercury News&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;font-size:13px;color:#555;margin:9px 0 3px 0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;&quot;&gt; &lt;span&gt;Posted:&lt;/span&gt; 06 Mar 2010 05:00 AM PST&lt;/p&gt; &lt;div style=&quot;margin:0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;div id=&quot;articleBody&quot; class=&quot;articleBody&quot;&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;articleViewerGroup&quot; id=&quot;articleViewerGroup&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;articleEmbeddedViewerBox&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://extras.mnginteractive.com/live/media/site568/2010/0305/20100305__santos2~1_VIEWER.JPG&quot;/&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://extras.mnginteractive.com/live/media/site568/2010/0305/20100305__santos1~1_VIEWER.JPG&quot;/&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;bodytext&quot;&gt;Once upon a time, Sergio Santos had time aplenty â to play golf, take camping trips, ski at Incline Village. Now his mountain condo has been sold, the fairways and putting greens are distant memories, and the president of the local chapter of the United Autoworkers in Fremont has been devoting every waking hour to just one thing:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Trying to keep the NUMMI auto plant from shutting down forever.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This week, success seemed more elusive than ever. Toyota said it was determined to close the fabled New United Motor Manufacturing Inc. plant April 1, cutting adrift its 4,700 employees and tens of thousands of vendors throughout the Bay Area and beyond. That seemed to deal Santos and his fellow members of the UAW Local 2244 a fatal blow. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&quot;With all of Toyota&#39;s quality-control problems right now, why abandon a world-class work force that wins awards, and just throw these people out of a job?&quot; he asked. &quot;Some employees have been here as long as 26 years, and building quality cars and trucks is all they&#39;ve ever known.&quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Toyota did say it would give $250 million in bonuses to help workers through the transition period. But Santos&#39; bigger battle seemed to be drawing to a close.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Q What&#39;s the mood now at NUMMI as the plant approaches shutdown?&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;A As we get close to March 31, people are feeling the reality starting to sink in. But at the same time, our efficiency rating has gone up six or seven points into the &lt;/p&gt;high 90s, which tells me that these workers are trying to show the company that they&#39;ve got a quality work force in place here, and it would be a shame to shut this plant down.&lt;p class=&quot;bodytextragright&quot;&gt;There&#39;s a lot of uncertainty. But our members are hoping that a delegation heading to Japan this week (Thursday) on our behalf will be able to get an extension at the very least. For now, people are still focused on their work and hopeful that this place can be saved somehow.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Q What would NUMMI&#39;s closing mean to the Bay Area&#39;s economy?&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;A With the loss of jobs for nearly 5,000 workers at the plant, along with 50,000 more throughout the state among suppliers and vendors, the closure would mean an economic tsunami for the Bay Area and beyond.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;bodytextragright&quot;&gt;And from janitors to people doing environmental cleaning at night, to people making truck beds in L.A. or seats in Livermore, you&#39;ll see families ripped apart, suicides and broken homes. And you&#39;ll have a lot of homes lost to foreclosure. A lot of our people have already stopped making payments on their homes because they know they might not be able to pay those mortgages going forward.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Q What has the relationship between NUMMI and the UAW been like over the years?&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;A It&#39;s been quite unique. We&#39;ve had eight successive contracts without any work stoppage. For example, in 2005 the company came to us in the middle of a contract saying insurance costs were too high, so our members agreed to help offset those costs. We rose to the occasion and ratified a modified contract to modify the insurance plan.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Q How did you end up as the local&#39;s president?&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;A I was first elected president about five years ago. I came up through the ranks after starting at NUMMI in 1991, working on the assembly line. I&#39;m originally from San Leandro, and my grandfather worked in the &#39;50s at an automotive plant where Eastmont Mall now sits. And my dad worked at the Fremont plan in the early &#39;60s, so I&#39;m a third-generation autoworker, one of only a handful at NUMMI today.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Q What else can be done to try and keep the plant open?&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;A We have a blue-ribbon commission headed by California Treasurer Bill Lockyer and UC-Berkeley professor Harley Shaiken, and their delegation is heading to Japan, giving Toyota reasons why they shouldn&#39;t close the plant down. At the very least, they should give us an extension so we&#39;d have time to try to figure things out, even if it comes to the union making concessions to keep it open. We just want Toyota to give us a chance.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;taglinejb&quot;&gt;Contact Patrick May at 408-920-5689.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;printinfobox&quot;&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;infoboxhead&quot;&gt;SERGIO SANTOS&lt;br/&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;infoboxtext&quot;&gt;Age: 46&lt;br/&gt;Birthplace: San Leandro &lt;br/&gt;Position: President of UAW Local 2244 &lt;br/&gt;Previous jobs: An assembly-line worker at NUMMI and before that an air-conditioning mechanic&lt;br/&gt;Education: San Jose City College &lt;br/&gt;Family: Fiancee, Marcella Velasco; daughter, Ashley, 22.&lt;br/&gt;Residence: Willow Glen &lt;br/&gt;Other interests: Golf, travel, camping, skiing, riding Harley-Davidson motorcycles, BBQ with the family, &quot;but I&quot;ve had no spare time to do any of that in the past three years.&quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p/&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;infoboxhead&quot;&gt;FIVE THINGS ABOUT SERGIO SANTOS&lt;br/&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;infoboxtext&quot;/&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;bold&quot;&gt;1. Quit college and took a job to help put his older brother through college.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;bold&quot;&gt;2. Is a third-generation auto worker.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;bold&quot;&gt;3. Has traveled to all 50 states.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;bold&quot;&gt;4. An avid bicyclist, he has often ridden from Willow Glen to Morgan Hill and back.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;bold&quot;&gt;5. Fell in love at first sight with his fiancee, Marcella, after asking her out of the blue to have coffee. Marcella, a real-estate agent, thought at first he wanted to buy a house, but he soon confessed he was &quot; lost inside her eyes and couldn&quot;t find my way out.&quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org&quot;&gt;Five Filters&lt;/a&gt; featured article: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://medialens.org/alerts/09/091216_chilcot_inquiry_the.php&quot;&gt;Chilcot Inquiry&lt;/a&gt;. Available tools: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/pdf-newspaper/&quot;&gt;PDF Newspaper&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/&quot;&gt;Full Text RSS&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/term-extraction/&quot;&gt;Term Extraction&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;image&quot;&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt; &lt;tr&gt; &lt;td style=&quot;margin-bottom:0;line-height:1.4em;&quot;&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;margin:1em 0 3px 0;&quot;&gt; &lt;a name=&quot;3&quot; style=&quot;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;font-size:18px;&quot; href=&quot;http://www.centralchronicle.com/viewnews.asp?articleID=28772&quot;&gt;Honda picks Rajasthan over Haryana - Central Chronicle&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;font-size:13px;color:#555;margin:9px 0 3px 0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;&quot;&gt; &lt;span&gt;Posted:&lt;/span&gt; 06 Mar 2010 04:39 AM PST&lt;/p&gt; &lt;div style=&quot;margin:0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;p&gt;Agencies&lt;br/&gt;Jaipur, Mar 6: &lt;br/&gt;After facing a series of labour unrest at its existing plant in Manesar, two-wheeler maker Honda Motorcycle &amp;amp; Scooter (HMSI) India Private Limited has finally decided to step out of Haryana for its second manufacturing facility. The auto major has selected Rajasthan for this facility with an initial investment of Rs 500 crore. &lt;br/&gt;The plant, spread across 60 acres near Bhiwadi, would have an initial capacity of 6 lakh vehicles per annum. The company intends to scale up its capacity to 12 lakh vehicles per annum after five years with an additional investment of Rs 600 crore. Bureau of Investment Promotion commissioner Purshottam Agarwal told ET that the state government has cleared the company&#39;s proposal. Bureau of Investment Promotion is Rajasthan government&#39;s investment promotion agency. &lt;br/&gt;&quot;We have offered them a customised package which includes land at concessional rate, cash subsidy on VAT, 50% subsidy on stamp duty, 50% concession on electricity duty and special rate of 0.05% on central sales tax. The civil work is likely to begin this month,&quot; he said. &lt;br/&gt;After roping in Honda Siel&#39;s second car plant in Khushkhera near Bhiwadi in 2008, this is the second big-ticket investment for Rajasthan in the automobile sector. &lt;br/&gt;&quot;The car plant of Honda Siel is one of the magnetic factors for the company to select Rajasthan for setting up its two-wheeler manufacturing facility in the state. It will help the company manage both plants in a better way. Another pulling factor is the Japan External Trade Organisation (JETRO) complex in Neemrana where dozens of Japanese companies have already set up shops. The HMSI plant will also attract various auto ancillary and accessory units that supply auto parts to this company,&quot; he said. &lt;br/&gt;Labour unrest at its existing plant too is said to have played a key role in prompting company to step out of Haryana. &lt;br/&gt;Incidentally, the company, in October last year, had threatened to shut down its factory at Manesar in Haryana and move to an alternate location after production fell by nearly 50% due to workers&#39; strike. This agitation had forced the HMSI management to give a salary hike of Rs 4,400 across the board besides special incentives as per respective remuneration structures. &lt;br/&gt;The company has so far invested Rs 1,300 crore in its plant at Manesar. It is expected to reach 100% capacity utilisation by 2010-11. &lt;br/&gt;The company expects a sale of 1.25 million vehicles this financial year and expects the figure to rise to 1.5 million next year. &quot;Apart from robust domestic sales, we export scooters and motorcycles to 35 countries including most of the countries of the European Union. To fulfill the growing demand, we needed the second manufacturing facility,&quot; said a company official. &lt;/p&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;p&gt;Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org&quot;&gt;Five Filters&lt;/a&gt; featured article: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://medialens.org/alerts/09/091216_chilcot_inquiry_the.php&quot;&gt;Chilcot Inquiry&lt;/a&gt;. The suspect was arrested on charges of petit theft with two prior theft convictions, resisting a retail merchant and battery with a prior conviction.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Police arrived to find the 34-year-old employee struggling with the suspect at the front door. The employee told police he saw the suspect try to leave Marshalls with items valued at $168. When he told her who he was, police said, she pushed him, punched him and bit him. Another employee told police he witnessed the incident.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;The suspect was with two other women who stole items in a bag, but they fled in a black sport utility vehicle, police said.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Sandy Strickland&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;DTI-ITAL&quot;&gt;The following are crimes and other incidents reported recently in Mandarin to the Jacksonville Sheriff&#39;s Office:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;DTI-BOLD&quot;&gt;Residential burglary:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;DTI-BOLD&quot;&gt;10700 block of Sky Lark Drive&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;DTI-BOLD&quot;&gt;-&lt;/span&gt; Someone came into the home of a 90-year-old woman and stole $67 from her wallet, which was hidden in a cabinet, police said.
