&lt;/li&gt; &lt;/ul&gt; &lt;table id=&quot;itemcontentlist&quot;&gt; &lt;tr xmlns=&quot;&quot;&gt; &lt;td style=&quot;margin-bottom:0;line-height:1.4em;&quot;&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;margin:1em 0 3px 0;&quot;&gt; &lt;a name=&quot;1&quot; style=&quot;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;font-size:18px;&quot; href=&quot;http://www.chillicothegazette.com/article/20100227/NEWS01/2270302/-1/newsfront2/Mobile-drives-emphasize-importance-of-blood-donations&quot;&gt;Mobile drives emphasize importance of blood donations - Chillico Gazette&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;font-size:13px;color:#555;margin:9px 0 3px 0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;&quot;&gt; &lt;span&gt;Posted:&lt;/span&gt; 27 Feb 2010 04:04 AM PST&lt;/p&gt; &lt;div style=&quot;margin:0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Message from fivefilters.org: If you can, please &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/#donate&quot;&gt;donate to the full-text RSS service&lt;/a&gt; so we can continue developing it.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;article-bodytext&quot; id=&quot;article-bodytext&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;p&gt;Local American Red Cross specialist John Williams knows just how important every pint of blood collected by the organization is.&lt;/p&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;p&gt;Williams&#39; life was saved after a motorcycle accident several years ago by blood provided by the agency, and that was when he decided to become involved with the Red Cross. In his work as a Specialist II, Williams travels daily for the Red Cross collecting blood donations.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&quot;It is very important to give, because you could be saving a life,&quot; he said.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Rodney Wilson, communications manager of the American Red Cross&#39; Central Ohio arm, said a constant, critical need for blood exists in the southern Ohio area. The First Capital District chapter of the organization was trying to help remedy some of the problem by collecting blood donations Friday in its mobile unit at Adena Regional Medical Center.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This month, the organization had to cancel 41 blood drives in the region because of bad weather, which resulted in 1,600 blood donations that couldn&#39;t be collected. Each donation has the potential to help as many as three people.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The greatest need right now, Wilson said, is for types O and B-negative blood.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The winter and summer months tend to be the most challenging seasons for blood donations. In the winter, people might have a hard time getting out to donate because of weather concerns or blood drive cancellations, and in the summer, school is out, eliminating school-based blood drives during a season when the number of auto accidents requiring blood assistance increases.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Donating blood is a painless procedure, beyond a brief feeling of being pinched, Wilson said, addressing what he thinks is a common misconception that keeps people away.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&quot;One of the main reasons I have heard people say they don&#39;t donate is because they are afraid of needles,&quot; he said.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The process takes about 10 minutes to complete.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Ashley Tainer-Harp, a medical professional herself, and her husband, Keith, donate regularly because they understand how important it is to give.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&quot;Honestly, more people really need to do this. My husband and I always donate through the Red Cross because we enjoy their staff and they make you feel comfortable while you are here,&quot; she said.&lt;/p&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org&quot;&gt;Five Filters&lt;/a&gt; featured article: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://medialens.org/alerts/09/091216_chilcot_inquiry_the.php&quot;&gt;Chilcot Inquiry&lt;/a&gt;. Available tools: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/pdf-newspaper/&quot;&gt;PDF Newspaper&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/&quot;&gt;Full Text RSS&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/term-extraction/&quot;&gt;Term Extraction&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;image&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt; &lt;tr&gt; &lt;td style=&quot;margin-bottom:0;line-height:1.4em;&quot;&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;margin:1em 0 3px 0;&quot;&gt; &lt;a name=&quot;2&quot; style=&quot;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;font-size:18px;&quot; href=&quot;http://www.bucyrustelegraphforum.com/article/20100227/SPORTS/2270310&quot;&gt;There is some hope for a drag strip in Mansfield - Bucyrus Telegraph Forum&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;font-size:13px;color:#555;margin:9px 0 3px 0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;&quot;&gt; &lt;span&gt;Posted:&lt;/span&gt; 27 Feb 2010 04:18 AM PST&lt;/p&gt; &lt;div style=&quot;margin:0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Message from fivefilters.org: If you can, please &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/#donate&quot;&gt;donate to the full-text RSS service&lt;/a&gt; so we can continue developing it.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;article-bodytext&quot; id=&quot;article-bodytext&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;p&gt;If this makes any sense, I&#39;m hopeful, but not really optimistic a drag strip is coming to Mansfield with its promises of jobs, tourism dollars and high entertainment.&lt;/p&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;p&gt;I guess I&#39;ve become jaded.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;How many rumors have I heard since expanding Mansfield Motorsports Park was first announced in the fall of 2006? I&#39;ve lost count.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Every time anyone sees movement on the property, it&#39;s assumed the project is back on and folks are wondering why the News Journal isn&#39;t publishing anything about it.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Dirt being moved from an expanding plant across the road on Ohio 13 to where the proposed drag strip would sit sent fans into a tizzy. Turns out it was just dirt being moved around.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;A couple years ago, I got hooked like a fish when track owner Mike Dzurilla told me the story about why there were little survey flags outlining where the track would be. He joked that he was marking gopher holes so fans wouldn&#39;t step in them and get hurt. When someone asked him how the holes happened to be in a straight line for almost a mile, Dzurilla winked and said, &quot;Smart gophers.&quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;I speculated in print that something could be afoot, but since I&#39;m writing this column, obviously nothing happened.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;A couple of years ago, I ran into Dzurilla in the infield during a race weekend at Mid-Ohio Sports Car Course. After the disappointment of seeing the drag strip get stalled by EPA issues then stopped by financing snafus -- on top of all the other issues swirling about the place at the time -- Dzurilla was still optimistic it would be built someday, but was far more cautious than usual.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;He jokingly offered me some advice that afternoon.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&quot;When the concrete trucks show up, you&#39;ll be the first one I call and you can sign your name,&quot; he said.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;I got the gist of what he was saying: Don&#39;t call us, we&#39;ll call you.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Last week my phone didn&#39;t ring. Instead, I saw a fax sitting on my desk from Carl Neutzling. He&#39;s a union guy who is helping spearhead a petition drive started by building trades, electrical workers and others who want to see the drag strip become a reality at MMP. The unions need the jobs that come with shovel-ready projects like this one.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The signatures will be given to Gov. Ted Strickland during a meeting in March with the hopes of Dzurilla getting a state grant to help with his financing for the $6- to $7-million expansion which is expected to bring at least 80 construction jobs, more than 20 permanent and 200 seasonal jobs and maybe 300,000 fans to town over the course of a racing season.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Dzurilla thinks the strip will enable him to open up the facility 200 or more days a year through rentals, car shows, motorcycle rallies, test-and-tunes, points racing and big events.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The extra dates and the many ways to use the facility would give him a margin of error he doesn&#39;t have right now. It&#39;s a business model TrueSports has used to keep Mid-Ohio Sports Car Course profitable through all the ups and downs of the motor sports world.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;With 200 dates in the books, every event no longer has to be an all-in gamble on whether a crowd will show up or the weather will hold up. He could conceivably bring back weekly racing to the oval and if things went well maybe even another NASCAR event.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&quot;What we have to do is expand the product line,&quot; Dzurilla told me last week, &quot;and that&#39;s what the drag strip does.&quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;It sounds swell, and I&#39;m hopeful. It&#39;s good that outsiders have taken the lead on reviving this project instead of Dzurilla doing it by himself, something he&#39;s been unable to do for almost four years.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;And despite it all, I&#39;m just not overly optimistic. I guess it&#39;s that jaded side which has been honed to a sharp edge from chasing rumors for too many years.&lt;/p&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;mailto:rmccurdy@nncogannett.com&quot;&gt;rmccurdy@nncogannett.com&lt;/a&gt;. 419-521-7241&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org&quot;&gt;Five Filters&lt;/a&gt; featured article: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://medialens.org/alerts/09/091216_chilcot_inquiry_the.php&quot;&gt;Chilcot Inquiry&lt;/a&gt;. href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/&quot;&gt;Full Text RSS&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/term-extraction/&quot;&gt;Term Extraction&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;image&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;span&gt;Posted:&lt;/span&gt; 27 Feb 2010 02:38 AM PST&lt;/p&gt; &lt;div style=&quot;margin:0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Message from fivefilters.org: If you can, please &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &lt;br /&gt;&amp;#13; &amp;#13; 2/27/2010&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;By the Salina Journal&amp;#13;&lt;/p&gt;&amp;#13;&amp;#13;&lt;p&gt;The names of finalists for a motorcycle and scooter being awarded as part of the 2009 Salina Area United Way campaign have been announced.&amp;#13;&lt;/p&gt;&amp;#13;&amp;#13;&lt;p&gt;Winners will be announced at the United Way&#39;s annual meeting, 11:30 a.m. to 1 p.m. Thursday at the Salina Country Club. Tickets to the meeting cost $15 a person, or 10 for $120, and may be purchased by contacting Brenda Gutierrez at 827-1312 or by e-mail, brenda@unitedway salina.org.&amp;#13;&lt;/p&gt;&amp;#13;&amp;#13;&lt;p&gt;Both the motorcycle and scooter were donated by Outlaw Cycles.&amp;#13;&lt;/p&gt;&amp;#13;&amp;#13;&lt;p&gt;To be eligible for the drawing for the 2008 Yamaha TT-R 125L motorcycle, donors had to pledge $52 or more to the United Way. From a field of 425 new donors, the names of eight finalists were drawn: Rick Couse, of Schwan&#39;s Global Supply Chain; Ron Legleiter, of UPS; Cherie Brigman, of the Salina School District; Allen Sims, of Exide Technologies; Mark Fuller, of Great Plains Manufacturing; Jason VanAtta, of Bergkamp; Darrin Wright, of the city of Salina; and Rebecca Pauley, of Salina Regional Health Center.&amp;#13;&lt;/p&gt;&amp;#13;&amp;#13;&lt;p&gt;To be eligible for the drawing for the 2009 Yamaha VINO Classic 49cc scooter, participants had to donate 1 percent of their annual salary. The six finalists are Patricia Owens, of Salina Regional Health Center; Patti Gendron, Dennis Saenger, Curtis Norris and Lynn Cooper, all of Advance Auto Parts Distribution Center; and James Waters, of Waters True Value, operations.&amp;#13;&lt;/p&gt;&amp;#13;&amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;div&gt;&amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &lt;b&gt;Join the Discussion:&lt;/b&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;i&gt;Salina.com&amp;#13; doesn&#39;t necessarily condone the comments here. &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://www.salina.com/tos/&quot;&gt;Read&lt;/a&gt; our&amp;#13; full online terms of service policy. &lt;/i&gt;&amp;#13; &amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&amp;#13; &amp;#13; &lt;/div&gt;&amp;#13; &amp;#13; &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org&quot;&gt;Five Filters&lt;/a&gt; featured article: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://medialens.org/alerts/09/091216_chilcot_inquiry_the.php&quot;&gt;Chilcot Inquiry&lt;/a&gt;. href=&quot;http://roadracingworld.com/news/article/?article=39546&quot;&gt;Peris Planning To Race Iron Horse BMW/ESP S1000 RR In AMA American ... - RoadracingWorld.com&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;font-size:13px;color:#555;margin:9px 0 3px 0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;&quot;&gt; &lt;span&gt;Posted:&lt;/span&gt; 26 Feb 2010 11:53 PM PST&lt;/p&gt; &lt;div style=&quot;margin:0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Message from fivefilters.org: If you can, please &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/#donate&quot;&gt;donate to the full-text RSS service&lt;/a&gt; so we can continue developing it.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div&gt; &lt;p class=&quot;date&quot;&gt;Feb 27, 2010, Â©Copyright 2010, Roadracing World Publishing, Inc.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h5&gt; &lt;p class=&quot;byline&quot;&gt;From a &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;press release&lt;/a&gt; issued by Syndicate Motorsport Managment:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;(Tucson, AZ) â Evan Steel Performance and Iron Horse BMW recently tested the BMW S1000RR Superbike in Arizona. The purpose of the test was to determine the competitiveness of the new BMW Superbike in the AMA American Superbike class. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; Like many teams going into the 2010 racing season, ESP was forced to suspend their racing efforts due to a lack of budget. Not wanting to watch the entire AMA series from home, the team started looking at other partnerships and opportunities that could see them participate in a few AMA Superbike rounds. That search brought them together with John and Jennifer Cartwright of Iron Horse Motorcycles, a Tucson, Arizona BMW dealer. Iron Horse BMW was looking to race one of their BMW S1000RR motorcycles to prove it&#39;s track worthiness to the local racer and track day crowd, a group of enthusiasts who might have overlooked the BMW in their search for a new ride. According to Cartwright, &quot;we have this great new product in the BMW S1000RR and we were looking for a way to introduce the bike to the sportbike crowd who may have never set foot inside a BMW dealer before.&quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; Cartwright rode an S1000RR across town to the ESP shop to inquire about taking one of his demo bikes to a track day. That conversation led to Evan Steel calling up former ESP rider Chris Peris to come down to a &#39;Take it to the Track&#39; event at the brand new Inde Motorsports Park in Wilcox, Arizona. Peris was familiar with the track, having set the motorcycle lap record there in recent months with a time of 1:55.60 on his AMA Superstock spec.--VIR podium finishing-- GSXR1000.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; The day of the test, Peris rode a bone stock BMW S1000RR, complete with headlights and all street equipment- minus the mirrors and passenger footpegs. The only performance enhancing equipment fitted to the bike was a set of racing slicks. In the first 15 lap session, Peris was getting a feel for the motorcycle and how it reacted when he turned up the pace. By the fifth lap of his second session, he bested the lap record by over a second, turning a 1:54.07. Evan stated, &quot;the bike was hugely impressive for a stock machine, the fact that Chris was able to lap faster on it than on his race bike is incredible!&quot; Chris added, &quot;Wow. I&#39;ve never ridden one of these new BMW&#39;s before, I can&#39;t believe I went faster on a stock bike with headlights, then I did on my own personal racebike. I can&#39;t wait to ride it after the ESP boys turn it into more of a racebike.&quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; Based on the strength of their first outing with the BMW S1000RR, Iron Horse Motorcycles and ESP have decided to join forces, creating Team Iron Horse BMW/ ESP for the upcoming AMA Superbike race in Fontana with Chris Peris riding. Although the team would like to contest the remaining AMA Superbike rounds, the budget is not currently in place. Team Iron Horse BMW/ ESP is actively seeking sponsorship to campaign as many additional AMA rounds as possible in 2010.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; For Sponsorship inquiries contact Murph at Syndicate Motorsport Management, LLC: &lt;br/&gt;&amp;#13; (+1) 831 464 3458 or email: murph@SyndicateRR.com&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;br/&gt;&amp;#13; Team Iron Horse BMW/ ESP&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; Win on Sunday, sell on Monday. Team Iron Horse BMW/ ESP was created to maximize the strengths of both organizations. Iron Horse BMW is focused on their customers&#39; ownership experience. ESP is an independent sport bike shop that focuses on the racer and track day rider. This is the reason Iron Horse BMW teamed up with ESP. ESP understands the sportbike market, and they have the skills and experience Iron Horse BMW needs to be able to sell the S1000RR to new customers with the knowledge only racing provides. Iron Horse BMW/ESP will use their racing experience to further develop the S1000RR. Team Iron Horse BMW/ ESP will use AMA Superbike competition to develop chassis, suspension and motor parts and accessories that will be made available to S1000RR owners, allowing them to enjoy the BMW S1000RR for years to come. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;br/&gt;&amp;#13; Evan Steel Performance&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; Evan Steel Performance is a small, personal, specialized shop located in Tucson, Arizona that deals with all aspects of motorcycle road racing. ESP bikes have had some of the highest trap speeds in their classes at AMA Nationals, as well as the highest top speed at start/finish at the 50th annual Macau Grand Prix. In 2009, ESP clinched the Supersport East title with numerous victories. In 2008, ESP scored a very rare privateer podium at the VIR AMA National in the Superstock class with Chris Peris. ESP is open to any level of racing, from basic race prep to planning a season at the Nationals.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; ESP can be reached at (520) 294 3050 or www.evansteelperformance.com&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;br/&gt;&amp;#13; Iron Horse BMW&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; Iron Horse BMW is Arizona&#39;s premier BMW dealer, located in Tucson, Arizona. Iron Horse is dedicated to providing their customers with the best possible ownership experience. The staff are passionate and avid motorcyclists from motocross to roadracing and everything in between. They have the experience and ability to help riders get the most out of their motorcycles. To make your dream of S1000RR ownership a reality, contact Iron Horse at (520)327-0773 or www.ironhorsemotorcycles.com&lt;/p&gt;&lt;br clear=&quot;left&quot;/&gt;&lt;br clear=&quot;left&quot;/&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;More Breaking Headlines&lt;/a&gt; | &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;Next Article&lt;/a&gt; | &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;Home&lt;/a&gt;&lt;p&gt;  &lt;/p&gt; &lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org&quot;&gt;Five Filters&lt;/a&gt; featured article: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://medialens.org/alerts/09/091216_chilcot_inquiry_the.php&quot;&gt;Chilcot Inquiry&lt;/a&gt;. &lt;td style=&quot;margin-bottom:0;line-height:1.4em;&quot;&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;margin:1em 0 3px 0;&quot;&gt; &lt;a name=&quot;1&quot; style=&quot;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;font-size:18px;&quot; href=&quot;http://www.autoblog.com/2010/02/26/robb-report-dubs-mercedes-sls-amg-2010-car-of-the-year-b/&quot;&gt;Robb Report dubs Mercedes SLS AMG 2010 Car of the Year, Bugatti Veyron ... - autoblog&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;font-size:13px;color:#555;margin:9px 0 3px 0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;&quot;&gt; &lt;span&gt;Posted:&lt;/span&gt; 26 Feb 2010 08:01 AM PST&lt;/p&gt; &lt;div style=&quot;margin:0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Message from fivefilters.org: If you can, please &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/#donate&quot;&gt;donate to the full-text RSS service&lt;/a&gt; so we can continue developing it.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;div id=&quot;pr_text&quot;&gt;&lt;strong&gt;ROBB REPORT EDITORS NAME MERCEDES-BENZ SLS AMG &quot;2010 CAR OF THE YEAR&quot;&lt;p&gt; AND BUGATTI VEYRON 16.4 GRAND SPORT &quot;CAR OF THE DECADE&quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;p&gt; Hitting newsstands today, Robb Report&#39;s March issue takes readers to Napa Valley for an insider&#39;s look at the luxury world&#39;s most exceptional new sports cars, sedans, and sport-utility vehicles.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt; MALIBU, CA (February 23, 2010)â For the first time in the 17-year history of Robb Report&#39;s &quot;Car of the Year&quot; competition, the panel of 50 VIP judges bestowed two honors, naming the Mercedes-Benz SLS AMG as &quot;2010 Car of the Year&quot; and the Bugatti Veyron 16.4 Grand Sport as &quot;Car of the Decade.&quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt; Robb Report&#39;s &quot;Car of the Year&quot; award is presented annually to an automobile, formally introduced in the previous year, whose technical designs, styling, and performance position it as the world&#39;s preeminent sports or luxury vehicle.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt; The selections resulted from extensive testing in California&#39;s Napa Valley by a panel of experts that included Robb Report editor in chief Brett Anderson, automotive editor Robert Ross, and correspondents Paul Dean and Paul Meyers. These journalists were joined by more than 50 privately invited guest judges, including executives and Robb Report readers.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt; An insider&#39;s look at this year&#39;s competition will be provided in the eagerly awaited March issue, which hits newsstands today. In addition, this date will mark the launch of &quot;RobbReport.TV,&quot; which will debut with stunning &quot;Car of the Year&quot; footage and on-the-scene impressions from members of the judging panel. A firsthand look at the action from Napa Valley will be accessible at http://robbreport.tv.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt; In earning &quot;Car of the Year&quot; honors for 2010, the Mercedes-Benz SLS AMG outdistanced 11 luxury and sports cars, topping the Audi R8 V10, Aston Martin DBS Volante, Lamborghini Gallardo LP 550-2 Valentino Balboni, Bentley Continental Supersports, Land Rover Range Rover Autobiography, Jaguar XKR, Porsche Panamera Turbo, Ford Shelby GT500 Super Snake, Allard J2X MkII, Spyker C8 Aileron, and BMW X6 M.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt; Recalling its 1950s predecessor, the new SLS AMG is a &quot;neoclassic,&quot; according to Mr. Dean. &quot;A superb melding of yesterday&#39;s styling with the technological sophistication of the 21st century, this new European idol steers precisely; has a peerless, powerful, and well-proven AMG power train with stronger pull than an Amtrak; and drives lighter than all its length, width, and tonnage might suggest.&quot; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt; Considered &quot;the most eagerly anticipated&quot; member of the class of 2010, the SLS AMG &quot;is a most deserving Car of the Year and does not disappoint in either the performance or panache departments,&quot; said Mr. Ross. &quot;The SLS is a substantive car in every respect.&quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt; The unprecedented decision to award winners for both the year and the decade &quot;was uniformly agreed upon by our judging panel, which determined that the $2 million Bugatti Veyron defied all categorization, thus deserving its own distinct honor,&quot; explained Mr. Anderson.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt; Establishing an entirely new precedent as &quot;Car of the Decade,&quot; the Bugatti Veyron 16.4 Grand Sport earned uniform praise from Robb Report&#39;s judging panel. &quot;The Bugatti&#39;s mission-to celebrate unapologetically beauty and power-placed this contender in an altogether different arena,&quot; Mr. Anderson explained. &quot;Over the course of our judging period, the Veyron 16.4 Grand Sport truly showcased mind-bending performance, while maintaining its ability to be imminently drivable. Such an impressive achievement is indeed a rarity.&quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt; These perceptions were affirmed by substantially all the judges as well as Mr. Ross, who was impressed by the Veyron&#39;s ability &quot;to push engineering and execution to levels of sophistication more befitting a complicated Swiss watch than a ground-going conveyance. The Grand Sport redefines what is possible, something no car has done since the McLaren F1 was introduced almost two decades ago.&quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Robb Report&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt; Now in its 34th year, Robb Report is the international authority and trusted journal of connoisseurship . Each month, the magazine reports on issues and trends affecting the affluent market, with coverage of exclusive events and features on exceptional automobiles, motorcycles, aircraft, art, jewelry, watches, fashion, travel, homes, wines, spirits, and cigars. Additional information can be accessed through the magazine&#39;s web site at www.robbreport.com.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org&quot;&gt;Five Filters&lt;/a&gt; featured article: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://medialens.org/alerts/09/091216_chilcot_inquiry_the.php&quot;&gt;Chilcot Inquiry&lt;/a&gt;. href=&quot;http://www.webwire.com/ViewPressRel.asp?aId=113345&quot;&gt;BMW NA Receives Two Green Building LEED Certificates - WebWire&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;font-size:13px;color:#555;margin:9px 0 3px 0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;&quot;&gt; &lt;span&gt;Posted:&lt;/span&gt; 26 Feb 2010 06:57 AM PST&lt;/p&gt; &lt;div style=&quot;margin:0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Message from fivefilters.org: If you can, please &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/#donate&quot;&gt;donate to the full-text RSS service&lt;/a&gt; so we can continue developing it.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;div id=&quot;content&quot;&gt; &lt;p&gt;Two of BMW NA&#39;s Regional Distribution Centers located in suburban Chicago (Minooka, IL) and Eastern Pennsylvania (Lower Nazareth, PA) have received LEED (Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design) certifications from the U.S. Green Building Council.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;According to LEED guidelines, both facilities were constructed in an environmental and sustainable way. Highlights include energy and water usage being reduced by more than 20 percent compared to standard building practice. Further, over 80 percent of all construction waste was recycled or otherwise diverted from landfills. Both facilities were noted for using recycled and locally sourced materials, drought tolerant landscaping, and eliminating permanent irrigation systems to reduce the use of potable water.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The facility in Lower Nazareth, PA received &quot;LEED certified&quot; recognition, while the facility in Minooka, IL was awarded &quot;LEED silver certified.&quot; Currently, the two centers serve 279 BMW and MINI dealers in the Northeast and Midwest with next-day delivery of auto and motorcycle parts, accessories and branded lifestyle products.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p id=&quot;wwguid&quot;&gt;WebWireID113345&lt;/p&gt; &lt;dl id=&quot;relatedLinks&quot;&gt;&lt;dt&gt;Related Links&lt;/dt&gt; &lt;dd&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://www.bmwusa.com/standard/content/experience/newsfeed/post/2010/02/25/BMW-NA-Receives-Two-Green-Building-LEED-Certificates.aspx&quot;&gt;Source&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/dd&gt; &lt;dd&gt;&lt;/dd&gt; &lt;dd&gt;&lt;/dd&gt; &lt;/dl&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;newsDisclaimer&quot;&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This news content was configured by WebWire editorial staff. &lt;img style=&quot;padding-top:6px&quot; alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://gmodules.com/ig/images/plus_google.gif&quot; /&gt; &lt;/a&gt; &lt;/h1&gt; &lt;/td&gt; &lt;td width=&quot;1%&quot; /&gt; &lt;/tr&gt; &lt;/table&gt; &lt;hr style=&quot;border:1px solid #ccc;padding:0;margin:0&quot; /&gt; &lt;ul style=&quot;clear:both;padding:0 0 0 1.2em;width:100%&quot; id=&quot;summarylist&quot;&gt; &lt;li&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;#1&quot;&gt;Taking a taxi isn&amp;rsquo;t always a ride in the park - MSNBC&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/li&gt; &lt;li&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;#2&quot;&gt;And they&#39;re off: auto show now open - Cincinnati.com&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/li&gt; &lt;li&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;#3&quot;&gt;Learn the basics of car care and more at Arts and Crafts Center - Ogden Standard-Examiner&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/li&gt; &lt;li&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;#4&quot;&gt;Help Wanted, Los Angeles: Seeking a Friendly Hard-Worker Who Has a ... - Insurance News Net&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/li&gt; &lt;/ul&gt; &lt;table id=&quot;itemcontentlist&quot;&gt; &lt;tr xmlns=&quot;&quot;&gt; &lt;td style=&quot;margin-bottom:0;line-height:1.4em;&quot;&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;margin:1em 0 3px 0;&quot;&gt; &lt;a name=&quot;1&quot; style=&quot;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;font-size:18px;&quot; href=&quot;http://www.msnbc.msn.com/id/35443481/ns/travel-tips/&quot;&gt;Taking a taxi isn&amp;rsquo;t always a ride in the park - MSNBC&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;font-size:13px;color:#555;margin:9px 0 3px 0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;&quot;&gt; &lt;span&gt;Posted:&lt;/span&gt; 25 Feb 2010 08:24 AM PST&lt;/p&gt; &lt;div style=&quot;margin:0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Message from fivefilters.org: If you can, please &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/#donate&quot;&gt;donate to the full-text RSS service&lt;/a&gt; so we can continue developing it.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;mR165&quot;&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;textBodyBlack&quot;&gt;&lt;span id=&quot;byLine&quot;&gt;Shana Graham was lucky. When the Seattle public relations exec was visiting India a few years ago, she hailed an auto rickshaw â one of those three-wheeled taxis lacking both doors and seat belts â and immediately found herself careening wildly through the streets. Her requests to slow down fell on deaf ears. &quot;The driver was clearly drunk,&quot; she recalls, &quot;and retorted, &#39;You Westerners, you have too much fear!&#39;&quot; As they sped into a traffic circle, he called back, &quot;Don&#39;t worry! Be happy!&quot; just before the rickshaw flattened, like a pancake, into a car.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;textBodyBlack&quot;&gt;&lt;span id=&quot;byLine&quot;&gt;Luckily, Graham walked away from the accident with only a few bruises. But it&#39;s a reminder of how a five-minute trip across town can either be a joyride or a descent into chaos.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;textBodyBlack&quot;&gt;&lt;span id=&quot;byLine&quot;&gt;Sure, every place has its share of scary cab drivers, but some places are worse than others. Bangkok, for instance, topped the &quot;most dangerous&quot; list of a recent Hotels.com taxi survey (though the city&#39;s cabbies also ranked as the fourth-most friendly). But the level of fright isn&#39;t always because of a rickety tuk-tuk. Depending on the location, there can be a risk of robbery, or the horror when you realize that your driver isn&#39;t watching the road but rather an episode of a reality show.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; name=&quot;storyContinued&quot; id=&quot;AdShowcase_F2&quot;&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;textBodyBlack&quot;&gt;&lt;span id=&quot;byLine&quot;&gt;Granted, most travelers who get in a cab upon landing at an airport or walking out of their hotel get nothing but an uneventful ride. And Alfred LaGasse, CEO of the Taxicab, Limousine and Paratransit Association, says that the industry is, for the most part, pretty consistent in the industrialized world.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;textBodyBlack&quot;&gt;&lt;span id=&quot;byLine&quot;&gt;He acknowledges, though, that there are some rough rides out there. &quot;The variations come,&quot; he says, &quot;with the kinds of regulations that countries choose to implement.&quot; Some countries have no regulations at all. In Lima, for instance, anyone with a car (or even a rental) can stick a taxi sign on the door and start picking up passengers â even if they have less of an idea where your hotel is than you do.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;textBodyBlack&quot;&gt;&lt;span id=&quot;byLine&quot;&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;textBodyBlack&quot;&gt;&lt;span id=&quot;byLine&quot;&gt;The scariest rides carry the threat of assault, robbery or even murder. But usually the greatest threat one faces from a bad cab is getting taken for a ride in the financial sense. In almost every city around the world â including the U.S. â unlicensed cabs can try to gouge passengers with inflated fares. The risk isn&#39;t just a high price, says LaGasse, but liability in an accident. &quot;With an illegal vehicle you have no protection whatsoever. Even if the driver carries personal insurance, that won&#39;t cover paying passengers.&quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;textBodyBlack&quot;&gt;&lt;span id=&quot;byLine&quot;&gt;When in doubt about which cab to use, consider these tips from LaGasse. First, make sure the cab is licensed â &quot;with a decal on the window or windshield and, generally speaking, a meter, though not always,&quot; he says. To plan ahead, call your hotel before you start a trip, and ask them what to look for and what kind of fare to expect from the airport.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;textBodyBlack&quot;&gt;&lt;span id=&quot;byLine&quot;&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;textBodyBlack&quot;&gt;&lt;span id=&quot;byLine&quot;&gt;Other world travelers have their own survival tips. Greg Poschman, an Aspen, Colo.-based director and photographer who travels a lot in developing nations, says he insists on seat belts and has even used nylon camera straps to rig his own. He also never sits in the front seat. &quot;Behind the driver is safest,&quot; he says, &quot;as he will instinctively steer to save himself in a wreck.&quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;textBodyBlack&quot;&gt;&lt;span id=&quot;byLine&quot;&gt;Sometimes, picking the right cabbie can actually bolster your security. When consultant Robert Longley was in Rio de Janiero during the 1990s, he and his wife had a taxi driver take them to see the rainforest. &quot;We got pulled over by a cop who wanted all of our money,&quot; he recalls. &quot;The taxi driver told him we were diplomats and that he would get into trouble if anything bad happened to us. The cop got on his motorcycle and left. We took our driver out for dinner that night.&quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;textBodyBlack&quot;&gt;&lt;span id=&quot;byLine&quot;&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;img width=&quot;100%&quot; height=&quot;0&quot;/&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org&quot;&gt;Five Filters&lt;/a&gt; featured article: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://medialens.org/alerts/09/091216_chilcot_inquiry_the.php&quot;&gt;Chilcot Inquiry&lt;/a&gt;. Available tools: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/pdf-newspaper/&quot;&gt;PDF Newspaper&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/&quot;&gt;Full Text RSS&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/term-extraction/&quot;&gt;Term Extraction&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;image&quot;&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt; &lt;tr&gt; &lt;td style=&quot;margin-bottom:0;line-height:1.4em;&quot;&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;margin:1em 0 3px 0;&quot;&gt; &lt;a name=&quot;2&quot; style=&quot;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;font-size:18px;&quot; href=&quot;http://news.cincinnati.com/article/20100225/BIZ01/2260324/And+they+re+off++auto+show+now+open&quot;&gt;And they&#39;re off: auto show now open - Cincinnati.com&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;font-size:13px;color:#555;margin:9px 0 3px 0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;&quot;&gt; &lt;span&gt;Posted:&lt;/span&gt; 25 Feb 2010 08:17 AM PST&lt;/p&gt; &lt;div style=&quot;margin:0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Message from fivefilters.org: If you can, please &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/#donate&quot;&gt;donate to the full-text RSS service&lt;/a&gt; so we can continue developing it.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;article-bodytext&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;p&gt;The Cincinnati Auto Expo starts today as eager dealers hope the showcase of their latest and greatest models will entice 2010 sales.&lt;/p&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;p&gt;Dealers hope the show will wow potential customers as a tentative economic recovery - which pushed Ford into profitability - begins to take hold.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Edward &quot;Ace&quot; Ammann, executive vice president of the Greater Cincinnati Automobile Dealers Association, said an industry rebound is inevitable, noting 8.5 million new cars were sold in 2009, down from the typical 14 to 15 million.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&quot;The auto industry is going to come back strong. There&#39;s a lot of pent up demand out there,&quot; he said. &quot;The auto show always creates a spike in showroom visits.&quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Visitors don&#39;t actually get to buy new cars at the expo, but dealers typically see sales jump after the show generates new excitement. Salespeople at the event are allowed to hand out business cards and make appointments at their dealerships to interested visitors, but aren&#39;t allowed to negotiate deals.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&quot;One of the benefits of the show is you can shop for all cars you&#39;re interested in under one roof and there&#39;s no pressure to buy,&quot; Ammann said.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;More than 30 automotive brands will showcase cars, trucks, SUVs, minivans and motorcycles, Missing will be Hummer, Saturn and Pontiac, which General Motors discontinued as part of its bankruptcy restructuring. Nissan has also bowed out auto shows this year, choosing other marketing avenues.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Organizers don&#39;t release attendance figures, but thousands are expected to visit the popular show, which has been an annual event at the convention center for 20 years.&lt;/p&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org&quot;&gt;Five Filters&lt;/a&gt; featured article: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://medialens.org/alerts/09/091216_chilcot_inquiry_the.php&quot;&gt;Chilcot Inquiry&lt;/a&gt;. &lt;p&gt;YONKERS, N.Y.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Honda, Subaru are &#39;best&#39; on &#39;Consumer Reports&#39; list&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Consumer Reports named Honda and Subaru best all-around vehicle-makers in its annual auto issue, marking the fourth consecutive year Honda won top marks from the influential magazine.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;The ratings are based on the magazine&#39;s average road-test scores and predicted reliability scores.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Honda and Subaru were followed by Toyota and Hyundai, then a tie between Nissan and Volkswagen. Chrysler fared worst.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Â &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;NEW YORK&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;4th-quarter earnings jump at Macy&#39;s, Target, Sears&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Three of the nation&#39;s largest retailers reported significant increases in earnings in the fourth quarter and said yesterday that they expected improvement to continue.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;For the quarter that ended Jan.30, Macy&#39;s CEO Terry Lundgren said the Cincinnati company&#39;s results were driven by a new local merchandising strategy, a 26.6 percent increase in online sales and a rebound at its luxury Bloomingdale&#39;s chain.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;But sales in the fourth quarter declined 1.1 percent, to $7.85 billion from $7.93billion in the year-earlier period. Macy&#39;s listed a $466million profit, or $1.10 a share, compared with a loss of $4.77 billion, or $11.33 a share, a year earlier, a result of a write-down in assets.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;At Minneapolis-based Target, fourth-quarter profit totaled $936 million, or $1.24 a share, compared with $609million, or 81 cents a share, in the year-earlier period. The discounter said sales increased 3.7 percent, to $19.7billion from $19billion.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Sears&#39; profit rose but sales slid $33 million to $13.2billion for the quarter. The decrease was the result of lower same-store sales and fewer full-line stores, the Hoffman Estates, Ill., company said.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Â &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;MARYSVILLE, OHIO&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Motorcycle plant reborn&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;as Honda parts center&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;The former Honda motorcycle plant in Marysville has begun its new life as a parts center for the adjoining auto-assembly plant.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Starting yesterday, Honda and an outside company, Midwest Express Inc., are working together to stage parts for use in the auto plant. The effort reduces the need to use delivery trucks.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;The former motorcycle plant has 11 new loading bays and is connected to the auto plant by an 800-foot tunnel.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;The motorcycle plant was active from 1979 to last year.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;- From staff, wire reports&lt;/p&gt; &amp;#13; &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org&quot;&gt;Five Filters&lt;/a&gt; featured article: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://medialens.org/alerts/09/091216_chilcot_inquiry_the.php&quot;&gt;Chilcot Inquiry&lt;/a&gt;. - The Auto Chanel&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;font-size:13px;color:#555;margin:9px 0 3px 0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;&quot;&gt; &lt;span&gt;Posted:&lt;/span&gt; 23 Feb 2010 11:50 PM PST&lt;/p&gt; &lt;div style=&quot;margin:0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Message from fivefilters.org: If you can, please &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/#donate&quot;&gt;donate to the full-text RSS service&lt;/a&gt; so we can continue developing it.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;div id=&quot;article-text&quot;&gt; &lt;br clear=&quot;all&quot;/&gt; &lt;p&gt;MELBOURNE â February 24, 2010: Aussie World Superbike rider Chris Vermeulen turned a few heads when he arrived at Phillip Island for pre-race testing prior to this weekend&#39;s season opener of the 2010 Superbike World Championship.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;While in Melbourne the former World Supersport Champion and MotoGP race-winner will be driving a 2010MY Chrysler 300C SRT8Â® which is powered by a 6.1-litre HEMIÂ® V-8 engine producing 317 kW and 569 Nm of torque.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;According to the motorcycle ace, it&#39;s a little more relaxed but no less exciting than his 300km/h factory Kawasaki superbike.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&quot;Getting around is a little more comfortable than normal with the 300C SRT8. The sound of the HEMI V-8 is just awesome,&quot; said Chris Vermeulen.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;For 2010, the Chrysler 300C SRT8 comes as standard with Remote Proximity Keyless Entry &amp;amp; Keyless Go. This allows the driver to open the door and start the car without needing to touch the key fob. Also now standard on all 300C V-8 models (5.7L and SRT8) is a Limited Slip Differential.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org&quot;&gt;Five Filters&lt;/a&gt; featured article: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://medialens.org/alerts/09/091216_chilcot_inquiry_the.php&quot;&gt;Chilcot Inquiry&lt;/a&gt;. Available tools: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/pdf-newspaper/&quot;&gt;PDF Newspaper&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; alt=&quot;image&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;This posting includes an audio/video/photo media file: &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.motorcyclenews.com/upload/204595/images/vermeulen(2).jpg&quot;&gt;Download Now&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;/div&gt; &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt; &lt;tr&gt; &lt;td style=&quot;margin-bottom:0;line-height:1.4em;&quot;&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;margin:1em 0 3px 0;&quot;&gt; &lt;a name=&quot;4&quot; style=&quot;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;font-size:18px;&quot; href=&quot;http://www.motorcycle-usa.com/764/6018/Motorcycle-Article/The-Rise-and-Fall-of-Husqvarna-Motorcycles.aspx&quot;&gt;The Rise and Fall of Husqvarna Motorcycles - Motorcycle USA&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;font-size:13px;color:#555;margin:9px 0 3px 0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;&quot;&gt; &lt;span&gt;Posted:&lt;/span&gt; 23 Feb 2010 11:28 PM PST&lt;/p&gt; &lt;div style=&quot;margin:0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Message from fivefilters.org: If you can, please &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/#donate&quot;&gt;donate to the full-text RSS service&lt;/a&gt; so we can continue developing it.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;div id=&quot;articleleftcolumn&quot;&gt;&amp;#13; &amp;#13; Husqvarna has wound a path filled with controversy, success and massive failures to its present-day position in the motorcycle world. It was sold out, bought out and nearly ground out, time and again. Yet it prevails. From an American standpoint,Â Husqvarna essentially bred off-road motorcycling in the US. It bore our heroes, our technology and the sporting competitiveness among motorcycle manufacturers and consumers that changed the entire industry. &lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; Like many old European brands, Husqvarna&#39;s history is steeped in armament. Originally founded in 1689 in the town of Huskvarna, the company produced weapons for the Swedish king, but once the fight was over, idle wartime production equipment was left seeking a new use, and that&#39;s how Husky transgressed into the motorcycle world. First it was hunting guns, then household appliances, white goods like stoves and sewing machines, and finally motorcycles and power equipment. Its first bike was produced in 1903 sourcing engines from other manufacturers. Thirty years later the company started road racing with its own V-Twins under the guidance of renowned engine-builder, Folke Mannerstedt. Like most brands at the time, off-road machines were nothing more than modified street bikes. This, combined with age restrictions, eventually led to unexpected success in the dirt. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; Motorcyclists had to be 18-years-old to ride, but bikes under 75 kilos (165 pounds) were deemed appropriate for riders aged 16 and up. Husqvarna first targeted the lightweight motorcycle realm with a 98cc moped, inadvertently starting down a path that would change off-road racing. In 1955, the &quot;Silverpilen,&quot; or &quot;Silver Arrow&quot; was introduced in Sweden with a 175cc motor and three-speed transmission. Consumers immediately began modifying the 2-stroke for off-road use, and by 1959 the factory produced five special machines for its racers which featured an enlarged 250cc engine and 4-speed tranny. Rolf Tibblin claimed the European 250Â &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://www.motorcycle-usa.com/117/Motorcycles/AMA-Motocross.aspx&quot;&gt;Motocross&lt;/a&gt; Championship that year and Husky began toying with a 500cc 4-stroke. But, for all intents and purposes, it was the 2-stroke design that launched Husky to fame. Husqvarna produced 100 replicas in 1963 which instantly sold out, and production began virtually doubling for the next several years. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&amp;#13; Fighting other European brands like Triumph, Bultaco, Maico, Greeves and CZ, Husky&#39;s critical advantage was the difference in weight. Success on the World Motocross GP circuit made for an easy transition into the American market where the sport of motocross was lagging. In January of 1966, Edison Dye imported two Husky 250 machines and gave them to Malcolm Smith and John Penton. In the fall of that same year, Dye brought over someone who could fully demonstrate the potential using the proper style and technique. Torsten Hallman won every race he entered in what came to be known as the 23-Moto Streak â an exhibition of superiority that ignited Americans&#39; imaginations and put Husqvarna on the map in the US. &lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; Penton took the role of East Coast distributor while Dye handled things on the Pacific side until 1974 when Husky took over. With sales and racing success in the States and abroad, Husqvarna&#39;s management was content to rest on its laurels, refusing to make a 125cc machine despite Penton and Dye&#39;s feverish requests for a small-bore. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; Husqvarna began constructing a new plant for its motorcycle production, called M73, but the vision was never realized. Swedish white goods powerhouse, Electrolux, purchased Husqvarna in 1977. Acquired for its line of appliances, Electrolux took on the motorcycles simply as part of the deal. After realizing the profit available in chainsaws, it headquartered that effort at M73. Motorcycles were split off into their own division,Â &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://www.motorcycle-usa.com/489/Motorcycles/Husqvarna-Motorcycles.aspx&quot;&gt;Husqvarna Motorcycles&lt;/a&gt; AB, and transferred nearly 50 miles away to a separate factory in Odeshog. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; Husqvarna became the target acquisition for Cagiva, a conglomerate owned at the time by the Castiglioni brothers, Gianfranco and Claudio, which made a habit of purchasing small European brands including Aermacchi, &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://www.motorcycle-usa.com/282/Motorcycles/Ducati-Motorcycles.aspx&quot;&gt;Ducati&lt;/a&gt;, Moto Morini and &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://www.motorcycle-usa.com/490/Motorcycles/MV-Agusta-Motorcycles.aspx&quot;&gt;MV Agusta&lt;/a&gt;. A young company with grandiose visions of its role in the world motorcycle economy, Cagiva purchased Husqvarna on April 1, 1986, taking complete control three months later and eventually moving the entire operation to Varese, Italy. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&amp;#13; From the time Cagiva took over operations of Husqvarna untilÂ &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://www.motorcycle-usa.com/274/Motorcycles/BMW-Motorcycles.aspx&quot;&gt;BMW&lt;/a&gt; bought the brand in 2007 were two of the darkest decades in Husky history. It was during this time that longstanding employees and loyal dealers started falling by the wayside. Unit sales dropped from the thousands into the hundreds, and a once-glorious brand was reduced to tatters. &lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; The 1990s were a decade of polar highs and lows. Though production was slow in the beginning, by 1993 it was beginning to pick up and Husqvarna came out of nowhere to win the World Motocross 500 GPs with Jacky Martins on a 4-stroke. However, by &#39;96, the company experienced its first year without producing any motorcycles. A year later, Gianfranco left to pursue the other Castiglioni business interests, leaving Claudio to handle the motorcycle side on his own, and from there the company underwent a series of financial changes. The buy-buy-buy attitude that had elevated Cagiva to the fifth-largest motorcycle manufacturer in the world, quickly switched to sell-sell-sell. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; Ducati and Moto Morini were off-loaded and the remaining Cagiva and Husqvarna brands were consolidated under the MV Agusta (MVA) label. In 2002, MVA filed for the Italian equivalent of Chapter 11 bankruptcy which it labored through for two years. Castiglioni&#39;s financial woes were temporarily eradicated when Malaysian auto maker, Proton, purchased a controlling 57.75% interest for 70 million Euro (approx $54 million). But just over a year later, fearing a complete bankruptcy by MVA, Proton decided it would be better to simply dump its share, selling the entire thing back to Italian investment company, Gevi SPA, for a single Euro ($1.19). &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; Once the Proton deal was complete, Husky/Cagiva/MV Agusta was again piloted by Castiglioni. Claudio made one final deal, this time much closer to home. BMW Motorrad purchased Husqvarna on July 19, 2007, and has been picking up the pieces ever since. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; Husqvarna&#39;s influence has reached countless riders. The list of heroes who rode Huskies at some point in their career is a Who&#39;s Who of motocross, enduro and desert racing legends. We spoke with men who played a role and witnessed first-hand the greatness, demise and resurgence of America&#39;s off-road racing heritage; men who designed, built, tested, raced and sold Husqvarna motorcycles. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/p&gt;&amp;#13; &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org&quot;&gt;Five Filters&lt;/a&gt; featured article: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://medialens.org/alerts/09/091216_chilcot_inquiry_the.php&quot;&gt;Chilcot Inquiry&lt;/a&gt;. href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/&quot;&gt;Full Text RSS&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/term-extraction/&quot;&gt;Term Extraction&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://thm-a01.yimg.com/nimage/1b15396e27c44086&quot; href=&quot;http://www.sunjournal.com/node/800087&quot;&gt;Olympics show why seat belts save lives - Sun-Journal&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;font-size:13px;color:#555;margin:9px 0 3px 0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;&quot;&gt; &lt;span&gt;Posted:&lt;/span&gt; 23 Feb 2010 08:19 AM PST&lt;/p&gt; &lt;div style=&quot;margin:0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Message from fivefilters.org: If you can, please &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/#donate&quot;&gt;donate to the full-text RSS service&lt;/a&gt; so we can continue developing it.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;primary_content&quot;&gt; &lt;p&gt;It&#39;s been more then 40 years since seat belts were first required in cars, and more than 25 years since a state, New York, first required people to use them.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Despite years of progress and legislation, it&#39;s remarkable that about one in five auto occupants still does not wear one.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Count 21-year-old Zachary Tenenbaum of Brunswick among them. He was thrown through the side window of a car Sunday when it rolled over on Route 9 in Durham.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;He survived, and should count himself a lucky man. The driver, Tevis Yarmala, 20, of Bowdoin did not require medical attention, no doubt because he was wearing a seat belt which kept him in the vehicle during the crash. The unbelted Tenenbaum, meanwhile, was hospitalized.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;We spend so many hours in motor vehicles, and they are now so comfortable, that it is impossible for most of us to imagine the violent potential of a crash or rollover even at moderate speeds.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;That&#39;s why watching the winter Olympics is, when you think about it, instructive.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Over the past 10 days, we have seen over and over what happens to a human body out of control. Some of the crashes on the downhill ski slopes have been frightening to watch as young men and women lose control at high speeds, sometimes in excess of 60 mph.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;While some skiers have been injured, most, fortunately, have walked away to compete again.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;But these crashes occur under ideal conditions. The competitors wear helmets, the area has been cleared of stationary obstacles and fences have been erected.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Unlike people thrown from cars during accidents, the skiers also aren&#39;t trying to dodge several tons of flying, rolling metal vehicle.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;The disturbing video of Georgian luger, Nodar Kumaritashvili, is sadly more representative of an automobile accident. The young man was thrown from his sled and directly into a steel beam.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Highways are lined with such objects, from trees to rocks, to bridge abutments, guardrails and, yes, steel beams. Most rollover victims are thrown into such an object, or crushed by a vehicle as it rolls.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Anyone who doesn&#39;t make a habit of wearing a seat belt is, as the Olympics and the statistics show, playing roulette with their life.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org&quot;&gt;Five Filters&lt;/a&gt; featured article: &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://medialens.org/alerts/09/091216_chilcot_inquiry_the.php&quot;&gt;Chilcot Inquiry&lt;/a&gt;. href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/&quot;&gt;Full Text RSS&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/term-extraction/&quot;&gt;Term Extraction&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;image&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; href=&quot;http://www.whowon.com/sResults.asp?SanctionID=377&amp;StoryID=284571&quot;&gt;Growing Field Preparing as Pre-Running Starts Saturday for 24th ... - Who Won&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;font-size:13px;color:#555;margin:9px 0 3px 0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;&quot;&gt; &lt;span&gt;Posted:&lt;/span&gt; 23 Feb 2010 04:59 AM PST&lt;/p&gt; &lt;div style=&quot;margin:0;font-family:Georgia,Helvetica,Arial,Sans-Serif;line-height:140%;font-size:13px;color:#FFFFFF;&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Message from fivefilters.org: If you can, please &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot; href=&quot;http://fivefilters.org/content-only/#donate&quot;&gt;donate to the full-text RSS service&lt;/a&gt; so we can continue developing it.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;spacer8&quot;&gt;Â &lt;/span&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;grey11&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Tuesday, February 23, 2010&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;text18&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Growing Field Preparing as Pre-Running Starts Saturday for 24th MasterCraft Safety Tecate SCORE San Felipe 250&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;spacer8&quot;&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;img width=&quot;320&quot; height=&quot;1&quot; align=&quot;center&quot;/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;spacer8&quot;&gt; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;grey11&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;by Dominic Clark&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;spacer8&quot;&gt; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;p align=&quot;left&quot;&gt;&lt;span id=&quot;intelliTxt&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;text12&quot;&gt;LOS ANGELES -- As pre-running over the rugged race course starts Saturday for next month&#39;s 24th Annual MasterCraft Safety Tecate SCORE San Felipe 250, a growing field that includes many of the world&#39;s best desert racers have entered this popular spring race. Attracting entries from 22 states and eight countries, the lineup includes a race-record 34 entries in SCORE Trophy-Truck, the marquee racing division for high-tech, 800-horsepower unlimited production trucks.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;Round 2 of the 2010 SCORE Desert Series will be held March 12-14 in Mexico&#39;s picturesque fishing village of San Felipe, located 120 miles south of the U.S. border on the East side of the Baja California peninsula along the azure waters of the tranquil Sea of Cortez.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;With nearly 275 entries expected, which would be in the top five in race history, competition will be held in 28 Pro and 6 Sportsman classes in the 232-mile race. The green flag will drop at 6 a.m. Pacific time on Saturday, March 13, for the motorcycle and ATV classes, followed three hours later by the car and truck classes at approximately 10 a.m. local time. The start and finish line for the race will once again be the landmark San Felipe Arches on Highway 5 on the outskirts of San Felipe. One vehicle will start every 30 seconds in the elapsed-time race, with a 10-hour time limit to become an official finisher.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;Following January&#39;s season-opening SCORE Laughlin Desert Challenge, the World&#39;s Foremost Desert Racing Series will visit Mexico for the first of three races in 2010.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&quot;This year&#39;s 24th MasterCraft Safety Tecate SCORE San Felipe 250 is quickly shaping up to be one of the top five races in the great history of this popular SCORE Baja race,&quot; said Sal Fish, SCORE CEO/President. &quot;SCORE has never had more cooperation from the Mexican authorities, the course is Baja spectacular and we are getting a superb entry listâall the ingredients that should add up to another amazing SCORE Baja race.&quot;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;This year&#39;s race will use a similar 232-mile race course as the past two years with a few modifications other than those caused by weather conditions. Running in a counter clockwise direction out of San Felipe up to and then parallel to Highway 3 (south side) and then south back down through three of the most picturesque and challenging washes in all of Baja.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;After the start at the landmark San Felipe Arches, the race will proceed north towards Zoo Road. The area approaching the Zoo Road crossing has been bladed again, which makes it a safer approach to the popular spectator area. That area will again be fenced, have grandstands and a jump and will be patrolled so that spectators can watch the action but not put themselves in way of the action.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;For the first time the course will travel east of instead of on the graded Morelia Road (after the Zoo Road junction) to the entrance to Matomi Wash. This will be one of the few times that SCORE will run through the majestic Matomi Wash before the other washes instead of following the others. After Matomi, the challenging course will run through two more of the infamous Baja canyonsâHuatomote and Chanate before heading back Northwest for the final sprint to the finish line.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;SCORE Trophy-Trucks have won 14 overalls in San Felipe in their 16-year history. Southern California&#39;s Mark Post/Jerry Whelchel in 1997 and San Diego&#39;s son/father team of Andy and Scott McMillin (2005) have the only two Class 1 wins since SCORE created the featured SCORE Trophy-Truck division in 1994.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;Both teams are now racing in SCORE Trophy-Truck where Post has two class and overall 4-wheel wins and the McMillins will be looking for their third consecutive SCORE Trophy-Truck race win and overall victory having won last year&#39;s season-ending Tecate SCORE Baja 1000 and this year&#39;s season-opening SCORE Laughlin Desert Challenge.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;In all nine of last year&#39;s 10 SCORE Trophy-Truck finishers are entered led by runner-up Robby Gordon, Charlotte, N.C., the NASCAR Cup team owner/driver who won last year&#39;s SCORE Trophy-Truck and SCORE Overall season point championship in the No. 1 Team Gordon Chevy CK1500.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;Post was third last year with Rob MacCachren (who will drive the No. 20 Chevy Sivlerado this year) in the No. 3 Ford F-150 while fourth was the team of Chet Huffman, Northridge, Calif./Jerry Welchel, Portola Hills, Calif. (No. 40 Chevy C1500) and fifth was Adam Householder, Orange, Calif. (No. 24 Chevy Silverado).&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;Sixth last year in SCORE Trophy-Truck was Las Vegas&#39; B.J. Baldwin (No. 97 Chevy Silverado) while the balance of the SCORE Trophy-Truck finishers were Las Vegas&#39; Troy Herbst (No. 49 Ford F-150), Robbie Pierce, Santee, Calif. (No. 30 Chevy Silverado), Greg Nunley, Visalia, Calif. (No. 10 Chevy Silverado) and Ed Stout, Santa Ana, Calif. (No. 13 Chevy Silverado).&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;Desert racers Ron Whitton of Arizona and Southern California&#39;s Robby Bell received the first starts for four-wheel and two-wheel vehicles in the computerized drawing for starting positions held Feb. 13. Whitton races in the featured SCORE Trophy-Truck division while Bell competes in Class 22 for open motorcycles.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;Drawing the first starting slot for the unlimited Class 1 open-wheel desert race cars was Germany&#39;s Armin Schwarz and teammate Martin Christensen, Escondido, Calif. Riding the first ATV off the line will be Class 25 team led by Wayne Matlock, El Cajon, Calif.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;With a race-record 34 entries so far in the marquee SCORE racing division for 800 horsepower, unlimited production trucks, Whitton, 66, owner of one of the largest plumbing contractor companies in Arizona, will lead a strong field in SCORE Trophy-Truck that features many of the world&#39;s top desert racers in the No. 39 Whitton Companies Ford F-150. Whitton, Mesa, Ariz., and his co-driver Chas Dana were fifth and 10th respectively in last year&#39;s Tecate SCORE Baja 500 and Tecate SCORE Baja 1000.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;Last year&#39;s overall motorcycle and ATV winners are entered this year. Last year&#39;s overall motorcycle champion was the Johnny Campbell Racing Honda team of Kendall Norman, Santa Barbara, Calif./Tim Weigand, Santa Clarita, Calif. on the No. 1x Honda CRF450X and the Overall ATV winners were the team of Wayne Matlock, El Cajon, Calif./Harold Goodman Jr., Brownstown, Mich./Josh Caster, El Cajon, Calif., on the No. 1a Honda TRX700X. Norman&#39;s team will start seventh in Motorcycles while Matlock&#39;s squad will be the first ATV off the line.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;Bell, 24, of Sun City, Calif., who left the factory Honda team at the end of 2008 after winning the two-wheel overall title in San Felipe three straight years (2006, 2007, 2008), returns to San Felipe for the first time since on a Kawasaki, leading a two-motorcycle Bruce Penhall Motorsports charge to Baja on the No. 2x Kawasaki KX450F. His co-rider, also a former Honda champion, is legendary SCORE Baja racer Steve Hengeveld, 34, Oak Hills, Calif., who was the overall San Felipe motorcycle winner for four straight year&#39;s with Honda icon Johnny Campbell (2001, 2002, 2003 and 2004).&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;Kawasaki will have factory-supported entries in San Felipe for this first time since 1996 and will attempt to break the JCR Honda dynasty which has won 12 of the last 13 SCORE San Felipe 250 races.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;In the first 23 years of this race, Honda has earned 14 overall motorcycle victories (including the last four years), Kawasaki has six, KTM has two and Husqvarna has one.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;As of today, SCORE Trophy-Truck had the most entries with 34, followed by the unlimited Class 1 with 19 and Class 1-2/1600 with 12. While 208 entries have been received to date, late registration will be accepted up until race morning and as many as 100 additional entries are expected.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;Among the motorcycle classes, the open Class 22 has the most vehicles entered to date with 11.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;Besides the K. Norman and Matlock teams, the other defending class winners entered this year are: Ronny Wilson, Long Beach, Calif. (Class 1), Mike Lawrence, Sunset Beach, Calif. (Class 10), Marc Burnett, Chula Vista, Calif. (Class 6), Jose Canchola Jr., Mexicali, Mexico (Class 7 but has switched to Class 6), Dave Crinklaw, Reedley, Calif. (Class 8), Eric Solorzano, Tijuana, Mexico (Class 11), Gavin Skilton, Anaheim, Calif. (Stock Mini), Mike Johnson, El Paso, Texas (Class 30), Jim O&#39;Neal, Simi Valley, Calif. (Class 50), Craig Christy, Burbank, Calif. (Class 24), Reid Rutherford, Montrose, Colo. (Class 26 but has switched to Class 7-2) and returning with SCORE Trophy-Truck regular Cameron Steele as rider of record is Brian Campbell, Bakersfield, Calif. (Class 40).&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;Christy, last season&#39;s SCORE Overall and Class 24 ATV season point champion, has also entered a team that he will lead this year in Class 25 as well, seeking a pair of class wins in San Felipe.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;Also returning this year to defend his Sportsman class race victory for the third straight year among those entered so far is Sportsman Car winner Peter Lang, Santa Rosa, Calif.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;The pre-race Manufacturer&#39;s Midway and tech inspection of the vehicles in the race will be held on Friday, March 12 from 10 a.m. to 6 p.m. on the picturesque Malecon, flanked by the Sea of Cortez on one side and the popular restaurants and night clubs of San Felipe on the other.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;At 10 a.m. on Sunday (March 14), the awards celebration will be held in front of The Beachcomber Night Club on the Malecon.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;At the 24th MasterCraft Safety Tecate SCORE San Felipe 250, MasterCraft Racing has entered not only company owner Robbie Pierce&#39;s No. 30 Chevy Silverado SCORE Trophy-Truck, but also the No. 20 Chevy Silverado SCORE Trophy-Truck to be driven by eight-time SCORE season class point champion Rob MacCachren of Las Vegas and the No. 42 Chevy Silverado driven by Will Staats, Valencia, Calif. All three trucks were built by prominent chassis builder Mike Julson&#39;s Jimco Racing Products of Santee, Calif. Julson is listed as a co-driver for both Pierce and MacCachren for this race, if needed.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;The MasterCraft racers will not be eligible to win any part of the special $10,000 MasterCraft Safety cash contingency bonus purse MasterCraft Safety has offered for this year&#39;s San Felipe race.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;In San Felipe, Pierce will start fourth, MacCachren 21st and Staats 25th in the massive SCORE Trophy-Truck field.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;A new attraction this year during the pre-running window will be the San Felipe Tequila Festival March 5-7.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;In addition to season class point championships, drivers in the Pro car and truck classes are also racing for part of the nearly $400,000 in cash purse and contingency postings as well as earn prestigious SCORE Toyota Milestone Awards given to all car and truck class drivers who complete every required mile of the five-race season. Being presented by Toyota Motorsports for the 25th consecutive year, a total of 59 drivers remain eligible after Round 1 of the 2010 SCORE Desert Series. Racers are also competing for the annual SCORE Off-Roadsman of the Year awards, including the MasterCraft Safety SCORE Rookie of the Year award.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;Current SCORE official annual sponsors are: BFGoodrich Tires-official tire, Volkswagen of America-official vehicle, Sunoco Race Fuels-official fuel supplier, Bilstein-official shock, Instant Mexico Auto Insurance-official Mexican auto insurance, Slime-official tire sealant and Red Bull-official energy drink. Associate sponsors are: Tecate Beer, Coca-Cola of Mexico, Las Vegas Events, MasterCraft Safety, Blue C Advertising, Off-Road, SignPros, P.C.I. Race Radios, McKenzie&#39;s Performance Products and Advanced Color Graphics.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br/&gt;Associate sponsors for the MasterCraft Safety Tecate SCORE San Felipe 250 are the Tourism and Convention Bureau of Mexicali/San Felipe and Cotuco.
